On\n// error of resolution, the controller is-rescheduled in an expedited manner\n// with an exponential back-off.\n//\n// m.lock must be held for writing\nfunc (m *Map) scheduleErrorResolver() {\n\tm.outstandingErrors = true\n\n\tif time.Since(m.errorResolverLastScheduled) <= errorResolverSchedulerMinInterval {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tm.errorResolverLastScheduled = time.Now()\n\n\tgo func() {\n\t\ttime.Sleep(errorResolverSchedulerDelay)\n\t\tmapControllers.UpdateController(m.controllerName(),\n\t\t\tcontroller.ControllerParams{\n\t\t\t\tGroup:       bpfMapSyncControllerGroup,\n\t\t\t\tDoFunc:      m.resolveErrors,\n\t\t\t\tRunInterval: errorResolverSchedulerMinInterval,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t)\n\t}()\n\n}\n\n// WithCache enables use of a cache. This will store all entries inserted from\n// user space in a local cache (map) and will indicate the status of each\n// individual entry.\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map {\n\tif m.cache == nil {\n\t\tm.cache = map[string]*cacheEntry{}\n\t}\n\tm.withValueCache = true\n\tm.enableSync = true\n\treturn m\n}\n\n// WithEvents enables use of the event buffer, if the buffer is enabled.\n// This stores all map events (i.e. add/update/delete) in a bounded event buffer.\n// If eventTTL is not zero, then events that are older than the TTL\n// will periodically be removed from the buffer.\n// Enabling events will use approx proportional to 100MB for every million capacity\n// in maxSize.\n//\n// TODO: The IPCache map have many periodic update events added by a controller for entries such as the 0.0.0.0/0 range.\n// These fill the event buffer with possibly unnecessary events.\n// We should either provide an option to aggregate these events, ignore hem from the ipcache event buffer or store them in a separate buffer.\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map {\n\tif !c.Enabled {\n\t\treturn m\n\t}\n\tm.Logger.Debug(\n\t\t\"enabling events buffer\",\n\t\tlogfields.Size, c.MaxSize,\n\t\tlogfields.TTL, c.TTL,\n\t)\n\tm.eventsBufferEnabled = true\n\tm.initEventsBuffer(c.MaxSize, c.TTL)\n\treturn m\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map {\n\tm.group = group\n\treturn m\n}\n\n// WithPressureMetricThreshold enables the tracking of a metric that measures\n// the pressure of this map. This metric is only reported if over the\n// threshold.\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map {\n\tif registry == nil {\n\t\treturn m\n\t}\n\n\t// When pressure metric is enabled, we keep track of map keys in cache\n\tif m.cache == nil {\n\t\tm.cache = map[string]*cacheEntry{}\n\t}\n\n\tm.pressureGauge = registry.NewBPFMapPressureGauge(m.NonPrefixedName(), threshold)\n\n\treturn m\n}\n\n// WithPressureMetric enables tracking and reporting of this map pressure with\n// threshold 0.\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map {\n\treturn m.WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry, 0.0)\n}\n\n// UpdatePressureMetricWithSize updates map pressure metric using the given map size.\nfunc (m *Map) UpdatePressureMetricWithSize(size int32) {\n\tif m.pressureGauge == nil {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// Do a lazy check of MetricsConfig as it is not available at map static\n\t// initialization.\n\tif !metrics.BPFMapPressure {\n\t\tif !m.withValueCache {\n\t\t\tm.cache = nil\n\t\t}\n\t\tm.pressureGauge = nil\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tpvalue := float64(size) / float64(m.MaxEntries())\n\tm.pressureGauge.Set(pvalue)\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) updatePressureMetric() {\n\t// Skipping pressure metric gauge updates for LRU map as the cache size\n\t// does not accurately represent the actual map size.\n\tif m.spec != nil && m.spec.Type == ebpf.LRUHash {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tm.UpdatePressureMetricWithSize(int32(len(m.cache)))\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int {\n\treturn m.m.FD()\n}\n\n// Name returns the basename of this map.\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string {\n\treturn m.name\n}\n\n// Path returns the path to this map on the filesystem.\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error) {\n\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn \"\", err\n\t}\n\n\treturn m.path, nil\n}\n\n// Unpin attempts to unpin (remove) the map from the filesystem.\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error {\n\tpath, err := m.Path()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\treturn os.RemoveAll(path)\n}\n\n// UnpinIfExists tries to unpin (remove) the map only if it exists.\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error {\n\tfound, err := m.exist()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tif !found {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\treturn m.Unpin()\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) controllerName() string {\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"bpf-map-sync-%s\", m.name)\n}\n\n// OpenMap opens the map at pinPath.\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error) {\n\tif !path.IsAbs(pinPath) {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"pinPath must be absolute: %s\", pinPath)\n\t}\n\n\tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(pinPath, nil)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\t// slogloggercheck: it's safe to use the default logger here as it has been initialized by the program up to this point.\n\tdefaultSlogLogger := logging.DefaultSlogLogger\n\n\tlogger := defaultSlogLogger.With(\n\t\tlogfields.BPFMapPath, pinPath,\n\t\tlogfields.BPFMapName, path.Base(pinPath),\n\t)\n\tm := &Map{\n\t\tLogger: logger,\n\t\tm:      em,\n\t\tname:   path.Base(pinPath),\n\t\tpath:   pinPath,\n\t\tkey:    key,\n\t\tvalue:  value,\n\t}\n\n\tm.updateMetrics()\n\tregisterMap(logger, pinPath, m)\n\n\treturn m, nil\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) setPathIfUnset() error {\n\tif m.path == \"\" {\n\t\tif m.name == \"\" {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"either path or name must be set\")\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tm.path = MapPath(m.Logger, m.name)\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// Recreate removes any pin at the Map's pin path, recreates and re-pins it.\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error {\n\tm.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n\n\tif m.m != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map already open: %s\", m.name)\n\t}\n\n\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tif err := os.Remove(m.path); err != nil && !errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist) {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"removing pinned map %s: %w\", m.name, err)\n\t}\n\n\tm.Logger.Info(\n\t\t\"Removed map pin, recreating and re-pinning map\",\n\t)\n\n\treturn m.openOrCreate(true)\n}\n\n// IsOpen returns true if the map has been opened.\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool {\n\tm.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n\treturn m.m != nil\n}\n\n// OpenOrCreate attempts to open the Map, or if it does not yet exist, create\n// the Map. If the existing map's attributes such as map type, key/value size,\n// capacity, etc. do not match the Map's attributes, then the map will be\n// deleted and reopened without any attempt to retain its previous contents.\n// If the map is marked as non-persistent, it will always be recreated.\n//\n// Returns whether the map was deleted and recreated, or an optional error.\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error {\n\tm.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n\n\treturn m.openOrCreate(true)\n}\n\n// CreateUnpinned creates the map without pinning it to the file system.\n//\n// TODO(tb): Remove this when all map creation takes MapSpec.\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error {\n\tm.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n\n\treturn m.openOrCreate(false)\n}\n\n// Create is similar to OpenOrCreate, but closes the map after creating or\n// opening it.\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error {\n\tif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\treturn m.Close()\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) openOrCreate(pin bool) error {\n\tif m.m != nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tif m.spec == nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attempted to create map %s without MapSpec\", m.name)\n\t}\n\n\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tm.spec.Flags |= GetMapMemoryFlags(m.spec.Type)\n\n\tif m.spec.InnerMap != nil {\n\t\tm.spec.InnerMap.Flags |= GetMapMemoryFlags(m.spec.InnerMap.Type)\n\t}\n\n\tif pin {\n\t\tm.spec.Pinning = ebpf.PinByName\n\t}\n\n\tem, err := OpenOrCreateMap(m.Logger, m.spec, path.Dir(m.path))\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tm.updateMetrics()\n\tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n\n\t// Consume the MapSpec.\n\tm.spec = nil\n\n\t// Retain the Map.\n\tm.m = em\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// Open opens the BPF map. All calls to Open() are serialized due to acquiring\n// m.lock\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error {\n\tm.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n\n\treturn m.open()\n}\n\n// open opens the BPF map. It is identical to Open() but should be used when\n// m.lock is already held. open() may only be used if m.lock is held for\n// writing.\nfunc (m *Map) open() error {\n\tif m.m != nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(m.path, nil)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"loading pinned map %s: %w\", m.path, err)\n\t}\n\n\tm.updateMetrics()\n\tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n\n\tm.m = em\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error {\n\tm.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n\n\tif m.enableSync {\n\t\tmapControllers.RemoveController(m.controllerName())\n\t}\n\n\tif m.m != nil {\n\t\tm.m.Close()\n\t\tm.m = nil\n\t}\n\n\tunregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error {\n\tvar duration *spanstat.SpanStat\n\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n\t\tduration = spanstat.Start()\n\t}\n\n\terr := m.m.NextKey(key, nextKeyOut)\n\n\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n\t\tmetrics.BPFSyscallDuration.WithLabelValues(metricOpGetNextKey, metrics.Error2Outcome(err)).Observe(duration.End(err == nil).Total().Seconds())\n\t}\n\n\treturn err\n}\n\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n\n// DumpWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given DumpCallback for\n// each map entry. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\n// retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n//\n// To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\n\tif cb == nil {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n\t}\n\n\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tm.lock.RLock()\n\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n\n\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n\tmk := m.key.New()\n\tmv := m.value.New()\n\n\ti := m.m.Iterate()\n\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n\t\tcb(mk, mv)\n\n\t\tmk = m.key.New()\n\t\tmv = m.value.New()\n\t}\n\n\treturn i.Err()\n}\n\n// DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\n// the slice of all values from all CPUs.\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\n// DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\n// DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\n// from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\n// to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\n\tif cb == nil {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n\t}\n\n\tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\", m.name)\n\t}\n\n\tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\n\tif !ok {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\", m.name)\n\t}\n\n\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tm.lock.RLock()\n\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n\n\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n\tmk := m.key.New()\n\tmv := v.NewSlice()\n\n\ti := m.m.Iterate()\n\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n\t\tcb(mk, mv)\n\n\t\tmk = m.key.New()\n\t\tmv = v.NewSlice()\n\t}\n\n\treturn i.Err()\n}\n\n// DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\n// if the given map does not exist.\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\n\tfound, err := m.exist()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tif found {\n\t\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\n// additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\n// element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\n// can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\n// In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\n// the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\n//\n// The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\n// object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\n// not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n\tif cb == nil {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n\t}\n\n\tif stats == nil {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n\t}\n\n\tvar (\n\t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n\t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n\t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n\t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n\n\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n\t)\n\n\tstats.start()\n\tdefer stats.finish()\n\n\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\n\t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\n\t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\n\tm.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n\tif m.m == nil {\n\t\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\n\t\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"map is closed\")\n\t}\n\n\t// Get the first map key.\n\tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\n\t\tstats.Lookup = 1\n\t\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n\t\t\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\n\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\n\t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\n\t// updated while being iterated)\n\tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\n\n\t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\n\t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\n\t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\n\tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\n\t\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\n\t\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\n\t\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\n\t\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\n\t\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\n\t\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\n\n\t\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\n\t\t\tstats.LookupFailed++\n\t\t\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\n\t\t\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\n\t\t\tif prevKeyValid {\n\t\t\t\tcurrentKey = prevKey\n\t\t\t\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\n\t\t\t\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\n\t\t\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n\t\t\t\tstats.KeyFallback++\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\n\t\t\t\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\n\t\t\t\t// one, or the first element in the map.\n\t\t\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n\t\t\t\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\n\t\t\t\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\n\t\t\t\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\n\t\t\t\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\n\t\t\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n\t\t\t\tstats.Interrupted++\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tcb(currentKey, value)\n\n\t\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\n\t\t\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n\t\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n\t\t\t\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn nextKeyErr\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\n\t\tprevKey = currentKey\n\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n\t\tprevKeyValid = true\n\t}\n\n\treturn ErrMaxLookup\n}\n\n// BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\n// of bpf maps.\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n\tm    *Map\n\terr  error\n\tkeys []KT\n\tvals []VT\n\n\tchunkSize      int\n\tmaxDumpRetries uint32\n\n\t// Iteration stats\n\tbatchSize int\n\n\topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\n}\n\n// NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\n// This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\n// when end of map is reached.\n// Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\n// the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\n// The pointer type of KT & VT must implement Map{Key,Value}, respectively.\n//\n// Subsequent iterations via IterateAll reset all internal state and begin\n// iteration over.\n//\n// Example usage:\n//\n//\tm := NewMap(\"cilium_test\",\n//\t\tebpf.Hash,\n//\t\t&TestKey{}, \t// *TestKey implements MapKey.\n//\t\t&TestValue{}, \t// *TestValue implements MapValue.\n//\t\tmapSize,\n//\t\tBPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n//\t)\n//\n//\titer := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\n//\tfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n//\t\t// ...\n//\t}\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n\treturn &BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]{\n\t\tm: m,\n\t}\n}\n\n// KeyPointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n// of a type T is a MapKey.\ntype KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n\tMapKey\n\t*T\n}\n\n// ValuePointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n// of a type T is a MapValue.\ntype ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n\tMapValue\n\t*T\n}\n\n// Err returns errors encountered during the previous iteration when\n// IterateAll(...) is called.\n//\n// If the iterator is reused, the error will be reset,\nfunc (kvs BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error {\n\treturn kvs.err\n}\n\nfunc (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\n\tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\n\t\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\n\t}\n\treturn defaultBatchedRetries\n}\n\nconst defaultBatchedRetries = 3\n\ntype BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] func(*BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n\n// WithEBPFBatchOpts returns a batch iterator option that allows for overriding\n// BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH options.\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n\t\tin.opts = opts\n\t\treturn in\n\t}\n}\n\n// WithMaxRetries returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the default\n// max batch retries.\n//\n// Unless the starting chunk size is set to be the map size, it is possible for iteration\n// to fail with ENOSPC if the passed allocated chunk array size is not big enough to accommodate\n// a the bpf maps underlying hashmaps bucket size.\n//\n// If this happens, BatchIterator will automatically attempt to double the batch size and\n// retry the iteration from the same place - up to a number of retries.\nfunc WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n\t\tin.maxDumpRetries = retries\n\t\treturn in\n\t}\n}\n\n// WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\n// chosen starting chunk size.\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n\t\tin.chunkSize = size\n\t\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\n\t\t\tin.chunkSize = 8\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn in\n\t}\n}\n\n// CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\n// iterator.\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\n\tc := 0\n\tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n\t\tc++\n\t}\n\treturn c, iter.Err()\n}\n\nfunc startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\n\tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\n\tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\n\treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\n}\n\n// IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\n// using the batched API.\n// In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\n// this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\n// of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\n// If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\n// will be returned via Err().\n//\n// All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\n//\n// If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will return the error that caused the failure.\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP] {\n\tswitch bi.m.Type() {\n\tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\n\t\tbreak\n\tdefault:\n\t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\", bi.m.Type())\n\t\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\n\t}\n\n\tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\n\n\tfor _, opt := range opts {\n\t\tif opt != nil {\n\t\t\tbi = opt(bi)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// reset values\n\tbi.err = nil\n\tbi.batchSize = 0\n\tbi.keys = {\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\n\titerate:\n\t\tfor {\n\t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n\t\t\t\tbi.err = ctx.Err()\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tretry:\n\t\t\tfor retry := range bi.maxBatchedRetries() {\n\t\t\t\t// Attempt to read batch into buffer.\n\t\t\t\tc, batchErr := bi.m.BatchLookup(&cursor, bi.keys, bi.vals, nil)\n\t\t\t\tbi.batchSize = c\n\n\t\t\t\tdone := errors.Is(batchErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\n\t\t\t\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\n\t\t\t\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\n\t\t\t\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\n\t\t\t\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\n\t\t\t\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\n\t\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t\t// If we receive ENOSPC failures, we will try to recover by growing the batch buffer\n\t\t\t\t// size (up to some max number of retries - default: 3) and retrying the iteration.\n\t\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t\t// [1] https://elixir.bootlin.com/linux/v6.12.6/source/kernel/bpf/hashtab.c#L1807-L1809\n\t\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t\t// Note: If this failure happens during the bpf syscall, it is expected that the underlying\n\t\t\t\t// cursor will not have been swapped - meaning that we can retry the iteration at the same cursor.\n\t\t\t\tif errors.Is(batchErr, unix.ENOSPC) {\n\t\t\t\t\tif retry == bi.maxBatchedRetries()-1 {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tbi.err = batchErr\n\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tbi.chunkSize *= 2\n\t\t\t\t\t\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n\t\t\t\t\t\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue retry\n\t\t\t\t} else if !done && batchErr != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\t// If we're not done, and we didn't hit a ENOSPC then stop iteration and record\n\t\t\t\t\t// the error.\n\t\t\t\t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"failed to iterate map: %w\", batchErr)\n\t\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\t// Yield all received pairs.\n\t\t\t\tfor i := range bi.batchSize {\n\t\t\t\t\tprocessed++\n\t\t\t\t\tif !yield(&bi.keys[i], &bi.vals[i]) {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\tif done {\n\t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tbreak retry // finish retry loop for this batch.\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// Dump returns the map (type map[string][]string) which contains all\n// data stored in BPF map.\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error {\n\tcallback := func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n\t\t// No need to deep copy since we are creating startingChunkSize(int(m.MaxEntries()))\n   152→\n   153→\t// Since we don't care about the actual data we just use a no-op binary\n   154→\t// decoder.\n   155→\tkeys := make(nopDecoder, chunkSize)\n   156→\tvals := make(nopDecoder, chunkSize)\n   157→\tmaxRetries := defaultBatchedRetries\n   158→\n   159→\tvar cursor ebpf.MapBatchCursor\n   160→\tfor {\n   161→\t\tfor retry := range maxRetries {\n   162→\t\t\t// Attempt to read batch into buffer.\n   163→\t\t\tc, batchErr := m.BatchLookup(&cursor, keys, vals, nil)\n   164→\t\t\tcount += c\n   165→\n   166→\t\t\tswitch {\n   167→\t\t\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\n   168→\t\t\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map. See full comment in\n   169→\t\t\t// [BatchIterator.IterateAll]\n   170→\t\t\tcase errors.Is(batchErr, unix.ENOSPC):\n   171→\t\t\t\tif retry == maxRetries-1 {\n   172→\t\t\t\t\terr = batchErr\n   173→\t\t\t\t} else {\n   174→\t\t\t\t\tchunkSize *= 2\n   175→\t\t\t\t}\n   176→\t\t\t\tkeys = make(nopDecoder, chunkSize)\n   177→\t\t\t\tvals = make(nopDecoder, chunkSize)\n   178→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   179→\t\t\tcase errors.Is(batchErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist):\n   180→\t\t\t\treturn\n   181→\t\t\tcase batchErr != nil:\n   182→\t\t\t\t// If we're not done, and we didn't hit a ENOSPC then stop iteration and record\n   183→\t\t\t\t// the error.\n   184→\t\t\t\terr = fmt.Errorf(\"failed to iterate map: %w\", batchErr)\n   185→\t\t\t\treturn\n   186→\t\t\t}\n   187→\t\t\t// Do the next batch\n   188→\t\t\tbreak\n   189→\t\t}\n   190→\t}\n   191→}\n   192→\n   193→func (m *Map) KeySize() uint32 {\n   194→\tif m.m != nil {\n   195→\t\treturn m.m.KeySize()\n   196→\t}\n   197→\tif m.spec != nil {\n   198→\t\treturn m.spec.KeySize\n   199→\t}\n   200→\treturn 0\n   201→}\n   202→\n   203→func (m *Map) ValueSize() uint32 {\n   204→\tif m.m != nil {\n   205→\t\treturn m.m.ValueSize()\n   206→\t}\n   207→\tif m.spec != nil {\n   208→\t\treturn m.spec.ValueSize\n   209→\t}\n   210→\treturn 0\n   211→}\n   212→\n   213→func (m *Map) MaxEntries() uint32 {\n   214→\tif m.m != nil {\n   215→\t\treturn m.m.MaxEntries()\n   216→\t}\n   217→\tif m.spec != nil {\n   218→\t\treturn m.spec.MaxEntries\n   219→\t}\n   220→\treturn 0\n   221→}\n   222→\n   223→func (m *Map) Flags() uint32 {\n   224→\tif m.m != nil {\n   225→\t\treturn m.m.Flags()\n   226→\t}\n   227→\tif m.spec != nil {\n   228→\t\treturn m.spec.Flags\n   229→\t}\n   230→\treturn 0\n   231→}\n   232→\n   233→func (m *Map) hasPerCPUValue() bool {\n   234→\tmt := m.Type()\n   235→\treturn mt == ebpf.PerCPUHash || mt == ebpf.PerCPUArray || mt == ebpf.LRUCPUHash || mt == ebpf.PerCPUCGroupStorage\n   236→}\n   237→\n   238→func (m *Map) updateMetrics() {\n   239→\tif m.group == \"\" {\n   240→\t\treturn\n   241→\t}\n   242→\tmetrics.UpdateMapCapacity(m.group, m.MaxEntries())\n   243→}\n   244→\n   245→// NewMap creates a new Map instance - object representing a BPF map\n   246→func NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n   247→\tmaxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map {\n   248→\n   249→\t// slogloggercheck: it's safe to use the default logger here as it has been initialized by the program up to this point.\n   250→\tdefaultSlogLogger := logging.DefaultSlogLogger\n   251→\tkeySize := reflect.TypeOf(mapKey).Elem().Size()\n   252→\tvalueSize := reflect.TypeOf(mapValue).Elem().Size()\n   253→\n   254→\treturn &Map{\n   255→\t\tLogger: defaultSlogLogger.With(\n   256→\t\t\tlogfields.BPFMapPath, name,\n   257→\t\t\tlogfields.BPFMapName, name,\n   258→\t\t),\n   259→\t\tspec: &ebpf.MapSpec{\n   260→\t\t\tType:       mapType,\n   261→\t\t\tName:       path.Base(name),\n   262→\t\t\tKeySize:    uint32(keySize),\n   263→\t\t\tValueSize:  uint32(valueSize),\n   264→\t\t\tMaxEntries: uint32(maxEntries),\n   265→\t\t\tFlags:      flags,\n   266→\t\t},\n   267→\t\tname:  path.Base(name),\n   268→\t\tkey:   mapKey,\n   269→\t\tvalue: mapValue,\n   270→\t\tgroup: name,\n   271→\t}\n   272→}\n   273→\n   274→// NewMapWithInnerSpec creates a new Map instance - object representing a BPF map with an inner map specification\n   275→func NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n   276→\tmaxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map {\n   277→\n   278→\t// slogloggercheck: it's safe to use the default logger here as it has been initialized by the program up to this point.\n   279→\tdefaultSlogLogger := logging.DefaultSlogLogger\n   280→\tkeySize := reflect.TypeOf(mapKey).Elem().Size()\n   281→\tvalueSize := reflect.TypeOf(mapValue).Elem().Size()\n   282→\n   283→\treturn &Map{\n   284→\t\tLogger: defaultSlogLogger.With(\n   285→\t\t\tlogfields.BPFMapPath, name,\n   286→\t\t\tlogfields.BPFMapName, name,\n   287→\t\t),\n   288→\t\tspec: &ebpf.MapSpec{\n   289→\t\t\tType:       mapType,\n   290→\t\t\tName:       path.Base(name),\n   291→\t\t\tKeySize:    uint32(keySize),\n   292→\t\t\tValueSize:  uint32(valueSize),\n   293→\t\t\tMaxEntries: uint32(maxEntries),\n   294→\t\t\tFlags:      flags,\n   295→\t\t\tInnerMap:   innerSpec,\n   296→\t\t},\n   297→\t\tname:  path.Base(name),\n   298→\t\tkey:   mapKey,\n   299→\t\tvalue: mapValue,\n   300→\t}\n   301→}\n   302→\n   303→func (m *Map) commonName() string {\n   304→\tif m.cachedCommonName != \"\" {\n   305→\t\treturn m.cachedCommonName\n   306→\t}\n   307→\n   308→\tm.cachedCommonName = extractCommonName(m.name)\n   309→\treturn m.cachedCommonName\n   310→}\n   311→\n   312→func (m *Map) NonPrefixedName() string {\n   313→\treturn strings.TrimPrefix(m.name, metrics.Namespace+\"_\")\n   314→}\n   315→\n   316→// scheduleErrorResolver schedules a periodic resolver controller that scans\n   317→// all BPF map caches for unresolved errors and attempts to resolve them. On\n   318→// error of resolution, the controller is-rescheduled in an expedited manner\n   319→// with an exponential back-off.\n   320→//\n   321→// m.lock must be held for writing\n   322→func (m *Map) scheduleErrorResolver() {\n   323→\tm.outstandingErrors = true\n   324→\n   325→\tif time.Since(m.errorResolverLastScheduled) <= errorResolverSchedulerMinInterval {\n   326→\t\treturn\n   327→\t}\n   328→\n   329→\tm.errorResolverLastScheduled = time.Now()\n   330→\n   331→\tgo func() {\n   332→\t\ttime.Sleep(errorResolverSchedulerDelay)\n   333→\t\tmapControllers.UpdateController(m.controllerName(),\n   334→\t\t\tcontroller.ControllerParams{\n   335→\t\t\t\tGroup:       bpfMapSyncControllerGroup,\n   336→\t\t\t\tDoFunc:      m.resolveErrors,\n   337→\t\t\t\tRunInterval: errorResolverSchedulerMinInterval,\n   338→\t\t\t},\n   339→\t\t)\n   340→\t}()\n   341→\n   342→}\n   343→\n   344→// WithCache enables use of a cache. This will store all entries inserted from\n   345→// user space in a local cache (map) and will indicate the status of each\n   346→// individual entry.\n   347→func (m *Map) WithCache() *Map {\n   348→\tif m.cache == nil {\n   349→\t\tm.cache = map[string]*cacheEntry{}\n   350→\t}\n   351→\tm.withValueCache = true\n   352→\tm.enableSync = true\n   353→\treturn m\n   354→}\n   355→\n   356→// WithEvents enables use of the event buffer, if the buffer is enabled.\n   357→// This stores all map events (i.e. add/update/delete) in a bounded event buffer.\n   358→// If eventTTL is not zero, then events that are older than the TTL\n   359→// will periodically be removed from the buffer.\n   360→// Enabling events will use approx proportional to 100MB for every million capacity\n   361→// in maxSize.\n   362→//\n   363→// TODO: The IPCache map have many periodic update events added by a controller for entries such as the 0.0.0.0/0 range.\n   364→// These fill the event buffer with possibly unnecessary events.\n   365→// We should either provide an option to aggregate these events, ignore hem from the ipcache event buffer or store them in a separate buffer.\n   366→func (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map {\n   367→\tif !c.Enabled {\n   368→\t\treturn m\n   369→\t}\n   370→\tm.Logger.Debug(\n   371→\t\t\"enabling events buffer\",\n   372→\t\tlogfields.Size, c.MaxSize,\n   373→\t\tlogfields.TTL, c.TTL,\n   374→\t)\n   375→\tm.eventsBufferEnabled = true\n   376→\tm.initEventsBuffer(c.MaxSize, c.TTL)\n   377→\treturn m\n   378→}\n   379→\n   380→func (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map {\n   381→\tm.group = group\n   382→\treturn m\n   383→}\n   384→\n   385→// WithPressureMetricThreshold enables the tracking of a metric that measures\n   386→// the pressure of this map. This metric is only reported if over the\n   387→// threshold.\n   388→func (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map {\n   389→\tif registry == nil {\n   390→\t\treturn m\n   391→\t}\n   392→\n   393→\t// When pressure metric is enabled, we keep track of map keys in cache\n   394→\tif m.cache == nil {\n   395→\t\tm.cache = map[string]*cacheEntry{}\n   396→\t}\n   397→\n   398→\tm.pressureGauge = registry.NewBPFMapPressureGauge(m.NonPrefixedName(), threshold)\n   399→\n   400→\treturn m\n   401→}\n   402→\n   403→// WithPressureMetric enables tracking and reporting of this map pressure with\n   404→// threshold 0.\n   405→func (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map {\n   406→\treturn m.WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry, 0.0)\n   407→}\n   408→\n   409→// UpdatePressureMetricWithSize updates map pressure metric using the given map size.\n   410→func (m *Map) UpdatePressureMetricWithSize(size int32) {\n   411→\tif m.pressureGauge == nil {\n   412→\t\treturn\n   413→\t}\n   414→\n   415→\t// Do a lazy check of MetricsConfig as it is not available at map static\n   416→\t// initialization.\n   417→\tif !metrics.BPFMapPressure {\n   418→\t\tif !m.withValueCache {\n   419→\t\t\tm.cache = nil\n   420→\t\t}\n   421→\t\tm.pressureGauge = nil\n   422→\t\treturn\n   423→\t}\n   424→\n   425→\tpvalue := float64(size) / float64(m.MaxEntries())\n   426→\tm.pressureGauge.Set(pvalue)\n   427→}\n   428→\n   429→func (m *Map) updatePressureMetric() {\n   430→\t// Skipping pressure metric gauge updates for LRU map as the cache size\n   431→\t// does not accurately represent the actual map size.\n   432→\tif m.spec != nil && m.spec.Type == ebpf.LRUHash {\n   433→\t\treturn\n   434→\t}\n   435→\tm.UpdatePressureMetricWithSize(int32(len(m.cache)))\n   436→}\n   437→\n   438→func (m *Map) FD() int {\n   439→\treturn m.m.FD()\n   440→}\n   441→\n   442→// Name returns the basename of this map.\n   443→func (m *Map) Name() string {\n   444→\treturn m.name\n   445→}\n   446→\n   447→// Path returns the path to this map on the filesystem.\n   448→func (m *Map) Path() (string, error) {\n   449→\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n   450→\t\treturn \"\", err\n   451→\t}\n   452→\n   453→\treturn m.path, nil\n   454→}\n   455→\n   456→// Unpin attempts to unpin (remove) the map from the filesystem.\n   457→func (m *Map) Unpin() error {\n   458→\tpath, err := m.Path()\n   459→\tif err != nil {\n   460→\t\treturn err\n   461→\t}\n   462→\n   463→\treturn os.RemoveAll(path)\n   464→}\n   465→\n   466→// UnpinIfExists tries to unpin (remove) the map only if it exists.\n   467→func (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error {\n   468→\tfound, err := m.exist()\n   469→\tif err != nil {\n   470→\t\treturn err\n   471→\t}\n   472→\n   473→\tif !found {\n   474→\t\treturn nil\n   475→\t}\n   476→\n   477→\treturn m.Unpin()\n   478→}\n   479→\n   480→func (m *Map) controllerName() string {\n   481→\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"bpf-map-sync-%s\", m.name)\n   482→}\n   483→\n   484→// OpenMap opens the map at pinPath.\n   485→func OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error) {\n   486→\tif !path.IsAbs(pinPath) {\n   487→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"pinPath must be absolute: %s\", pinPath)\n   488→\t}\n   489→\n   490→\tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(pinPath, nil)\n   491→\tif err != nil {\n   492→\t\treturn nil, err\n   493→\t}\n   494→\n   495→\t// slogloggercheck: it's safe to use the default logger here as it has been initialized by the program up to this point.\n   496→\tdefaultSlogLogger := logging.DefaultSlogLogger\n   497→\n   498→\tlogger := defaultSlogLogger.With(\n   499→\t\tlogfields.BPFMapPath, pinPath,\n   500→\t\tlogfields.BPFMapName, path.Base(pinPath),\n   501→\t)\n   502→\tm := &Map{\n   503→\t\tLogger: logger,\n   504→\t\tm:      em,\n   505→\t\tname:   path.Base(pinPath),\n   506→\t\tpath:   pinPath,\n   507→\t\tkey:    key,\n   508→\t\tvalue:  value,\n   509→\t}\n   510→\n   511→\tm.updateMetrics()\n   512→\tregisterMap(logger, pinPath, m)\n   513→\n   514→\treturn m, nil\n   515→}\n   516→\n   517→func (m *Map) setPathIfUnset() error {\n   518→\tif m.path == \"\" {\n   519→\t\tif m.name == \"\" {\n   520→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"either path or name must be set\")\n   521→\t\t}\n   522→\n   523→\t\tm.path = MapPath(m.Logger, m.name)\n   524→\t}\n   525→\n   526→\treturn nil\n   527→}\n   528→\n   529→// Recreate removes any pin at the Map's pin path, recreates and re-pins it.\n   530→func (m *Map) Recreate() error {\n   531→\tm.lock.Lock()\n   532→\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   533→\n   534→\tif m.m != nil {\n   535→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map already open: %s\", m.name)\n   536→\t}\n   537→\n   538→\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n   539→\t\treturn err\n   540→\t}\n   541→\n   542→\tif err := os.Remove(m.path); err != nil && !errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist) {\n   543→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"removing pinned map %s: %w\", m.name, err)\n   544→\t}\n   545→\n   546→\tm.Logger.Info(\n   547→\t\t\"Removed map pin, recreating and re-pinning map\",\n   548→\t)\n   549→\n   550→\treturn m.openOrCreate(true)\n   551→}\n   552→\n   553→// IsOpen returns true if the map has been opened.\n   554→func (m *Map) IsOpen() bool {\n   555→\tm.lock.Lock()\n   556→\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   557→\treturn m.m != nil\n   558→}\n   559→\n   560→// OpenOrCreate attempts to open the Map, or if it does not yet exist, create\n   561→// the Map. If the existing map's attributes such as map type, key/value size,\n   562→// capacity, etc. do not match the Map's attributes, then the map will be\n   563→// deleted and reopened without any attempt to retain its previous contents.\n   564→// If the map is marked as non-persistent, it will always be recreated.\n   565→//\n   566→// Returns whether the map was deleted and recreated, or an optional error.\n   567→func (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error {\n   568→\tm.lock.Lock()\n   569→\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   570→\n   571→\treturn m.openOrCreate(true)\n   572→}\n   573→\n   574→// CreateUnpinned creates the map without pinning it to the file system.\n   575→//\n   576→// TODO(tb): Remove this when all map creation takes MapSpec.\n   577→func (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error {\n   578→\tm.lock.Lock()\n   579→\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   580→\n   581→\treturn m.openOrCreate(false)\n   582→}\n   583→\n   584→// Create is similar to OpenOrCreate, but closes the map after creating or\n   585→// opening it.\n   586→func (m *Map) Create() error {\n   587→\tif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n   588→\t\treturn err\n   589→\t}\n   590→\treturn m.Close()\n   591→}\n   592→\n   593→func (m *Map) openOrCreate(pin bool) error {\n   594→\tif m.m != nil {\n   595→\t\treturn nil\n   596→\t}\n   597→\n   598→\tif m.spec == nil {\n   599→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attempted to create map %s without MapSpec\", m.name)\n   600→\t}\n   601→\n   602→\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n   603→\t\treturn err\n   604→\t}\n   605→\n   606→\tm.spec.Flags |= GetMapMemoryFlags(m.spec.Type)\n   607→\n   608→\tif m.spec.InnerMap != nil {\n   609→\t\tm.spec.InnerMap.Flags |= GetMapMemoryFlags(m.spec.InnerMap.Type)\n   610→\t}\n   611→\n   612→\tif pin {\n   613→\t\tm.spec.Pinning = ebpf.PinByName\n   614→\t}\n   615→\n   616→\tem, err := OpenOrCreateMap(m.Logger, m.spec, path.Dir(m.path))\n   617→\tif err != nil {\n   618→\t\treturn err\n   619→\t}\n   620→\n   621→\tm.updateMetrics()\n   622→\tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n   623→\n   624→\t// Consume the MapSpec.\n   625→\tm.spec = nil\n   626→\n   627→\t// Retain the Map.\n   628→\tm.m = em\n   629→\n   630→\treturn nil\n   631→}\n   632→\n   633→// Open opens the BPF map. All calls to Open() are serialized due to acquiring\n   634→// m.lock\n   635→func (m *Map) Open() error {\n   636→\tm.lock.Lock()\n   637→\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   638→\n   639→\treturn m.open()\n   640→}\n   641→\n   642→// open opens the BPF map. It is identical to Open() but should be used when\n   643→// m.lock is already held. open() may only be used if m.lock is held for\n   644→// writing.\n   645→func (m *Map) open() error {\n   646→\tif m.m != nil {\n   647→\t\treturn nil\n   648→\t}\n   649→\n   650→\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n   651→\t\treturn err\n   652→\t}\n   653→\n   654→\tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(m.path, nil)\n   655→\tif err != nil {\n   656→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"loading pinned map %s: %w\", m.path, err)\n   657→\t}\n   658→\n   659→\tm.updateMetrics()\n   660→\tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n   661→\n   662→\tm.m = em\n   663→\n   664→\treturn nil\n   665→}\n   666→\n   667→func (m *Map) Close() error {\n   668→\tm.lock.Lock()\n   669→\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   670→\n   671→\tif m.enableSync {\n   672→\t\tmapControllers.RemoveController(m.controllerName())\n   673→\t}\n   674→\n   675→\tif m.m != nil {\n   676→\t\tm.m.Close()\n   677→\t\tm.m = nil\n   678→\t}\n   679→\n   680→\tunregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n   681→\n   682→\treturn nil\n   683→}\n   684→\n   685→func (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error {\n   686→\tvar duration *spanstat.SpanStat\n   687→\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n   688→\t\tduration = spanstat.Start()\n   689→\t}\n   690→\n   691→\terr := m.m.NextKey(key, nextKeyOut)\n   692→\n   693→\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n   694→\t\tmetrics.BPFSyscallDuration.WithLabelValues(metricOpGetNextKey, metrics.Error2Outcome(err)).Observe(duration.End(err == nil).Total().Seconds())\n   695→\t}\n   696→\n   697→\treturn err\n   698→}\n   699→\n   700→type DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n   701→\n   702→// DumpWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given DumpCallback for\n   703→// each map entry. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\n   704→// retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n   705→//\n   706→// To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\n   707→func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\n   708→\tif cb == nil {\n   709→\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n   710→\t}\n   711→\n   712→\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n   713→\t\treturn err\n   714→\t}\n   715→\n   716→\tm.lock.RLock()\n   717→\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n   718→\n   719→\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n   720→\tmk := m.key.New()\n   721→\tmv := m.value.New()\n   722→\n   723→\ti := m.m.Iterate()\n   724→\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n   725→\t\tcb(mk, mv)\n   726→\n   727→\t\tmk = m.key.New()\n   728→\t\tmv = m.value.New()\n   729→\t}\n   730→\n   731→\treturn i.Err()\n   732→}\n   733→\n   734→// DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\n   735→// the slice of all values from all CPUs.\n   736→type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n   737→\n   738→// DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\n   739→// DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\n   740→// from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\n   741→// to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n   742→func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\n   743→\tif cb == nil {\n   744→\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n   745→\t}\n   746→\n   747→\tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\n   748→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\", m.name)\n   749→\t}\n   750→\n   751→\tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\n   752→\tif !ok {\n   753→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\", m.name)\n   754→\t}\n   755→\n   756→\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n   757→\t\treturn err\n   758→\t}\n   759→\n   760→\tm.lock.RLock()\n   761→\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n   762→\n   763→\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n   764→\tmk := m.key.New()\n   765→\tmv := v.NewSlice()\n   766→\n   767→\ti := m.m.Iterate()\n   768→\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n   769→\t\tcb(mk, mv)\n   770→\n   771→\t\tmk = m.key.New()\n   772→\t\tmv = v.NewSlice()\n   773→\t}\n   774→\n   775→\treturn i.Err()\n   776→}\n   777→\n   778→// DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\n   779→// if the given map does not exist.\n   780→func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\n   781→\tfound, err := m.exist()\n   782→\tif err != nil {\n   783→\t\treturn err\n   784→\t}\n   785→\n   786→\tif found {\n   787→\t\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\n   788→\t}\n   789→\n   790→\treturn nil\n   791→}\n   792→\n   793→// DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\n   794→// additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\n   795→// element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\n   796→// can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\n   797→// In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\n   798→// the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\n   799→//\n   800→// The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\n   801→// object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\n   802→// not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\n   803→func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n   804→\tif cb == nil {\n   805→\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n   806→\t}\n   807→\n   808→\tif stats == nil {\n   809→\t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n   810→\t}\n   811→\n   812→\tvar (\n   813→\t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n   814→\t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n   815→\t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n   816→\t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n   817→\n   818→\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n   819→\t)\n   820→\n   821→\tstats.start()\n   822→\tdefer stats.finish()\n   823→\n   824→\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n   825→\t\treturn err\n   826→\t}\n   827→\n   828→\t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\n   829→\t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\n   830→\t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\n   831→\tm.lock.Lock()\n   832→\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n   833→\tif m.m == nil {\n   834→\t\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\n   835→\t\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\n   836→\t\treturn errors.New(\"map is closed\")\n   837→\t}\n   838→\n   839→\t// Get the first map key.\n   840→\tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\n   841→\t\tstats.Lookup = 1\n   842→\t\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n   843→\t\t\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\n   844→\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n   845→\t\t\treturn nil\n   846→\t\t}\n   847→\t}\n   848→\n   849→\t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\n   850→\t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\n   851→\t// updated while being iterated)\n   852→\tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\n   853→\n   854→\t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\n   855→\t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\n   856→\t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\n   857→\tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\n   858→\t\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\n   859→\t\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\n   860→\t\t//\n   861→\t\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\n   862→\t\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\n   863→\t\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\n   864→\t\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\n   865→\t\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\n   866→\n   867→\t\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\n   868→\t\t\tstats.LookupFailed++\n   869→\t\t\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\n   870→\t\t\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\n   871→\t\t\tif prevKeyValid {\n   872→\t\t\t\tcurrentKey = prevKey\n   873→\t\t\t\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\n   874→\t\t\t\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\n   875→\t\t\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n   876→\t\t\t\tstats.KeyFallback++\n   877→\t\t\t} else {\n   878→\t\t\t\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\n   879→\t\t\t\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\n   880→\t\t\t\t// one, or the first element in the map.\n   881→\t\t\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n   882→\t\t\t\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\n   883→\t\t\t\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\n   884→\t\t\t\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\n   885→\t\t\t\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\n   886→\t\t\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n   887→\t\t\t\tstats.Interrupted++\n   888→\t\t\t}\n   889→\t\t\tcontinue\n   890→\t\t}\n   891→\n   892→\t\tcb(currentKey, value)\n   893→\n   894→\t\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\n   895→\t\t\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n   896→\t\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n   897→\t\t\t\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\n   898→\t\t\t}\n   899→\t\t\treturn nextKeyErr\n   900→\t\t}\n   901→\n   902→\t\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\n   903→\t\tprevKey = currentKey\n   904→\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n   905→\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n   906→\t\tprevKeyValid = true\n   907→\t}\n   908→\n   909→\treturn ErrMaxLookup\n   910→}\n   911→\n   912→// BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\n   913→// of bpf maps.\n   914→type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n   915→\tm    *Map\n   916→\terr  error\n   917→\tkeys []KT\n   918→\tvals []VT\n   919→\n   920→\tchunkSize      int\n   921→\tmaxDumpRetries uint32\n   922→\n   923→\t// Iteration stats\n   924→\tbatchSize int\n   925→\n   926→\topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\n   927→}\n   928→\n   929→// NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\n   930→// This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\n   931→// when end of map is reached.\n   932→// Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\n   933→// the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\n   934→// The pointer type of KT & VT must implement Map{Key,Value}, respectively.\n   935→//\n   936→// Subsequent iterations via IterateAll reset all internal state and begin\n   937→// iteration over.\n   938→//\n   939→// Example usage:\n   940→//\n   941→//\tm := NewMap(\"cilium_test\",\n   942→//\t\tebpf.Hash,\n   943→//\t\t&TestKey{}, \t// *TestKey implements MapKey.\n   944→//\t\t&TestValue{}, \t// *TestValue implements MapValue.\n   945→//\t\tmapSize,\n   946→//\t\tBPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n   947→//\t)\n   948→//\n   949→//\titer := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\n   950→//\tfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n   951→//\t\t// ...\n   952→//\t}\n   953→func NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n   954→\treturn &BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]{\n   955→\t\tm: m,\n   956→\t}\n   957→}\n   958→\n   959→// KeyPointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n   960→// of a type T is a MapKey.\n   961→type KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n   962→\tMapKey\n   963→\t*T\n   964→}\n   965→\n   966→// ValuePointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n   967→// of a type T is a MapValue.\n   968→type ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n   969→\tMapValue\n   970→\t*T\n   971→}\n   972→\n   973→// Err returns errors encountered during the previous iteration when\n   974→// IterateAll(...) is called.\n   975→//\n   976→// If the iterator is reused, the error will be reset,\n   977→func (kvs BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error {\n   978→\treturn kvs.err\n   979→}\n   980→\n   981→func (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\n   982→\tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\n   983→\t\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\n   984→\t}\n   985→\treturn defaultBatchedRetries\n   986→}\n   987→\n   988→const defaultBatchedRetries = 3\n   989→\n   990→type BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] func(*BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n   991→\n   992→// WithEBPFBatchOpts returns a batch iterator option that allows for overriding\n   993→// BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH options.\n   994→func WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n   995→\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n   996→\t\tin.opts = opts\n   997→\t\treturn in\n   998→\t}\n   999→}\n  1000→\n  1001→// WithMaxRetries returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the default\n  1002→// max batch retries.\n  1003→//\n  1004→// Unless the starting chunk size is set to be the map size, it is possible for iteration\n  1005→// to fail with ENOSPC if the passed allocated chunk array size is not big enough to accommodate\n  1006→// a the bpf maps underlying hashmaps bucket size.\n  1007→//\n  1008→// If this happens, BatchIterator will automatically attempt to double the batch size and\n  1009→// retry the iteration from the same place - up to a number of retries.\n  1010→func WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n  1011→\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n  1012→\t\tin.maxDumpRetries = retries\n  1013→\t\treturn in\n  1014→\t}\n  1015→}\n  1016→\n  1017→// WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\n  1018→// chosen starting chunk size.\n  1019→func WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n  1020→\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n  1021→\t\tin.chunkSize = size\n  1022→\t\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\n  1023→\t\t\tin.chunkSize = 8\n  1024→\t\t}\n  1025→\t\treturn in\n  1026→\t}\n  1027→}\n  1028→\n  1029→// CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\n  1030→// iterator.\n  1031→func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\n  1032→\tc := 0\n  1033→\tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n  1034→\t\tc++\n  1035→\t}\n  1036→\treturn c, iter.Err()\n  1037→}\n  1038→\n  1039→func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\n  1040→\tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\n  1041→\tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\n  1042→\treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\n  1043→}\n  1044→\n  1045→// IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\n  1046→// using the batched API.\n  1047→// In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\n  1048→// this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\n  1049→// of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\n  1050→// If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\n  1051→// will be returned via Err().\n  1052→//\n  1053→// All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\n  1054→//\n  1055→// If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will return the error that caused the failure.\n  1056→func (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP] {\n  1057→\tswitch bi.m.Type() {\n  1058→\tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\n  1059→\t\tbreak\n  1060→\tdefault:\n  1061→\t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\", bi.m.Type())\n  1062→\t\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\n  1063→\t}\n  1064→\n  1065→\tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\n  1066→\n  1067→\tfor _, opt := range opts {\n  1068→\t\tif opt != nil {\n  1069→\t\t\tbi = opt(bi)\n  1070→\t\t}\n  1071→\t}\n  1072→\n  1073→\t// reset values\n  1074→\tbi.err = nil\n  1075→\tbi.batchSize = 0\n  1076→\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n  1077→\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n  1078→\n  1079→\tprocessed := 0\n  1080→\tvar cursor ebpf.MapBatchCursor\n  1081→\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {\n  1082→\t\tif bi.Err() != nil {\n  1083→\t\t\treturn\n  1084→\t\t}\n  1085→\n  1086→\titerate:\n  1087→\t\tfor {\n  1088→\t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n  1089→\t\t\t\tbi.err = ctx.Err()\n  1090→\t\t\t\treturn\n  1091→\t\t\t}\n  1092→\t\tretry:\n  1093→\t\t\tfor retry := range bi.maxBatchedRetries() {\n  1094→\t\t\t\t// Attempt to read batch into buffer.\n  1095→\t\t\t\tc, batchErr := bi.m.BatchLookup(&cursor, bi.keys, bi.vals, nil)\n  1096→\t\t\t\tbi.batchSize = c\n  1097→\n  1098→\t\t\t\tdone := errors.Is(batchErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\n  1099→\t\t\t\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\n  1100→\t\t\t\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\n  1101→\t\t\t\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\n  1102→\t\t\t\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\n  1103→\t\t\t\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\n  1104→\t\t\t\t//\n  1105→\t\t\t\t// If we receive ENOSPC failures, we will try to recover by growing the batch buffer\n  1106→\t\t\t\t// size (up to some max number of retries - default: 3) and retrying the iteration.\n  1107→\t\t\t\t//\n  1108→\t\t\t\t// [1] https://elixir.bootlin.com/linux/v6.12.6/source/kernel/bpf/hashtab.c#L1807-L1809\n  1109→\t\t\t\t//\n  1110→\t\t\t\t// Note: If this failure happens during the bpf syscall, it is expected that the underlying\n  1111→\t\t\t\t// cursor will not have been swapped - meaning that we can retry the iteration at the same cursor.\n  1112→\t\t\t\tif errors.Is(batchErr, unix.ENOSPC) {\n  1113→\t\t\t\t\tif retry == bi.maxBatchedRetries()-1 {\n  1114→\t\t\t\t\t\tbi.err = batchErr\n  1115→\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n  1116→\t\t\t\t\t\tbi.chunkSize *= 2\n  1117→\t\t\t\t\t\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n  1118→\t\t\t\t\t\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n  1119→\t\t\t\t\t}\n  1120→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue retry\n  1121→\t\t\t\t} else if !done && batchErr != nil {\n  1122→\t\t\t\t\t// If we're not done, and we didn't hit a ENOSPC then stop iteration and record\n  1123→\t\t\t\t\t// the error.\n  1124→\t\t\t\t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"failed to iterate map: %w\", batchErr)\n  1125→\t\t\t\t\treturn\n  1126→\t\t\t\t}\n  1127→\n  1128→\t\t\t\t// Yield all received pairs.\n  1129→\t\t\t\tfor i := range bi.batchSize {\n  1130→\t\t\t\t\tprocessed++\n  1131→\t\t\t\t\tif !yield(&bi.keys[i], &bi.vals[i]) {\n  1132→\t\t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n  1133→\t\t\t\t\t}\n  1134→\t\t\t\t}\n  1135→\n  1136→\t\t\t\tif done {\n  1137→\t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n  1138→\t\t\t\t}\n  1139→\t\t\t\tbreak retry // finish retry loop for this batch.\n  1140→\t\t\t}\n  1141→\t\t}\n  1142→\t}\n  1143→}\n  1144→\n  1145→// Dump returns the map (type map[string][]string) which contains all\n  1146→// data stored in BPF map.\n  1147→func (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error {\n  1148→\tcallback := func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n  1149→\t\t// No need to deep copy since we are creating strings.\n  1150→\t\thash[key.String()] = append(hash[key.String()], value.String())\n  1151→\t}\n  1152→\n  1153→\tif err := m.DumpWithCallback(callback); err != nil {\n  1154→\t\treturn err\n  1155→\t}\n  1156→\n  1157→\treturn nil\n  1158→}\n  1159→\n  1160→// BatchLookup returns the count of elements in the map by dumping the map\n  1161→// using batch lookup.\n  1162→func (m *Map) BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any, opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error) {\n  1163→\treturn m.m.BatchLookup(cursor, keysOut, valuesOut, opts)\n  1164→}\n  1165→\n  1166→// DumpIfExists dumps the contents of the map into hash via Dump() if the map\n  1167→// file exists\n  1168→func (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error {\n  1169→\tfound, err := m.exist()\n  1170→\tif err != nil {\n  1171→\t\treturn err\n  1172→\t}\n  1173→\n  1174→\tif found {\n  1175→\t\treturn m.Dump(hash)\n  1176→\t}\n  1177→\n  1178→\treturn nil\n  1179→}\n  1180→\n  1181→func (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error) {\n  1182→\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n  1183→\t\treturn nil, err\n  1184→\t}\n  1185→\n  1186→\tm.lock.RLock()\n  1187→\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n  1188→\n  1189→\tvar duration *spanstat.SpanStat\n  1190→\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n  1191→\t\tduration = spanstat.Start()\n  1192→\t}\n  1193→\n  1194→\tvalue := m.value.New()\n  1195→\terr := m.m.Lookup(key, value)\n  1196→\n  1197→\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n  1198→\t\tmetrics.BPFSyscallDuration.WithLabelValues(metricOpLookup, If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\n   799→//\n   800→// The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\n   801→// object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\n   802→// not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\n   803→func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n   804→\tif cb == nil {\n   805→\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n   806→\t}\n   807→\n   808→\tif stats == nil {\n   809→\t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n   810→\t}\n   811→\n   812→\tvar (\n   813→\t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n   814→\t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n   815→\t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n   816→\t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n   817→\n   818→\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n   819→\t)\n   820→\n   821→\tstats.start()\n   822→\tdefer stats.finish()\n   823→\n   824→\tif err := m.Open();   929→// NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\n   930→// This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\n   931→// when end of map is reached.\n   932→// Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\n   933→// the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\n   934→// The pointer type of KT & VT must The callback function must\n// not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n\tif cb == nil {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n\t}\n\n\tif stats == nil {\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n\t}\n\n\tvar (\n\t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n\t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n\t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n\t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n\n\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n\t)\n\n\tstats.start()\n\tdefer stats.finish()\n\n\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\n\t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\n\t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\n\tm.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n\tif m.m == nil {\n\t\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\n\t\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\n\t\treturn errors.New(\"map is closed\")\n\t}\n\n\t// Get the first map key.\n\tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\n\t\tstats.Lookup = 1\n\t\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n\t\t\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\n\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\n\t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\n\t// updated while being iterated)\n\tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\n\n\t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\n\t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\n\t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\n\tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\n\t\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. The `Map` type is the primary interface for all map operations, wrapping the lower-level ebpf-go library with Cilium-specific functionality including caching, event streaming, pinning, and metrics.\n\nAll eBPF maps are stored in a BPF filesystem (bpffs) and can be persisted between program runs through pinning.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1.
