[Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n5. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n6. [Event System](#event-system)\n7. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n8. [Caching and Synchronization](#caching-and-synchronization)\n9. [Per-CPU Maps](#per-cpu-maps)\n10. [Advanced Features](#advanced-features)\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Type and Creation\n\n### Map Structure\n\nThe `Map` type is the main interface for working with eBPF maps:\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    Logger *slog.Logger\n    // ... internal fields\n}\n```\n\n#### Map Type Queries\n\n```go\n// Type returns the eBPF map type (Hash, LRUHash, Array, etc.)\nfunc (m *Map) Type() ebpf.MapType\n\n// KeySize returns the size of map keys in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) KeySize() uint32\n\n// ValueSize returns the size of map values in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) ValueSize() uint32\n\n// MaxEntries returns the maximum capacity of the map\nfunc (m *Map) MaxEntries() uint32\n\n// Flags returns the map creation flags\nfunc (m *Map) Flags() uint32\n\n// Name returns the basename of this map\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string\n\n// FD returns the file descriptor of the opened map\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int\n\n// IsOpen returns whether the map has been opened\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\n### Creating Maps\n\n#### NewMap\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new Map instance with the given parameters. The map is not yet created in the kernel; it remains in an uninitialized state until `Open()`, `OpenOrCreate()`, or `Create()` is called.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: The map name used for pinning and identification\n- `mapType`: The eBPF map type (e.g., `ebpf.Hash`, `ebpf.LRUHash`, `ebpf.Array`)\n- `mapKey`: A pointer to a sample map key (implements `MapKey`)\n- `mapValue`: A pointer to a sample map value (implements `MapValue`)\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum capacity of the map\n- `flags`: Creation flags (e.g., `unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_connections\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &ConnectionKey{},\n    &ConnectionValue{},\n    10000,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n)\n```\n\n#### NewMapWithInnerSpec\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a map with an inner map specification, used for maps of maps (e.g., for tail calls).\n\n### Opening and Creating Maps\n\n#### Open\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens an existing pinned map from the filesystem. If the map doesn't exist or cannot be opened, an error is returned. This call is idempotent—calling it multiple times on an already-open map succeeds without error.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires exclusive write lock for serialization\n- Loads the map from its pinned path\n- Automatically sets up metrics collection\n- Registers the map internally\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Failed to open map:\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n#### OpenOrCreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nAttempts to open an existing pinned map. If the map doesn't exist, creates and pins it. If an existing map is found but its attributes (type, key size, value size, capacity, flags) are incompatible, the old map is deleted and recreated.\n\n**Behavioral Details:**\n- Returns nil if the map was already open\n- Maps marked as non-persistent are always recreated\n- Automatically adds memory allocation flags based on map type\n- Sets `ebpf.PinByName` pinning flag during creation\n- Consumes the MapSpec after successful creation (cannot be reused)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\n// Create or reuse existing map\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Failed to open or create map:\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n#### Create\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nSimilar to `OpenOrCreate()` but closes the map after creation. Use this when you only need to create the map for initialization but don't intend to use it immediately.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `OpenOrCreate()` internally\n- Closes the map after successful creation\n- Useful for map initialization in startup hooks\n\n#### CreateUnpinned\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates the map without pinning it to the filesystem. The map exists only for the lifetime of the process.\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Temporary maps used only within a single process\n- Maps created for testing\n- Maps that are not meant to persist across restarts\n\n#### Recreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves any pinned map at the map's path, then creates and re-pins a new map. This is useful for forcing a fresh start of a map, clearing all previous entries.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Fails if the map is already open\n- Removes the old pin if it exists\n- Creates a new map and pins it\n\n**Example:**\n```go\n// Start fresh, discarding any previous entries\nif err := m.Recreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Failed to recreate map:\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n#### Close\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the map, releasing the file descriptor and unregistering it internally. After calling Close(), the map can be reopened by calling Open() or OpenOrCreate() again.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Idempotent—closing an already-closed map succeeds\n- Stops any active error resolution controller if caching is enabled\n- Unregisters the map from internal tracking\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nRetrieves the value associated with the given key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if the key is not found\n- Thread-safe with read-locking\n- Metrics collection is automatic if enabled\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 42}\nvalue, err := m.Lookup(key)\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n        fmt.Println(\"Key not found\")\n    } else {\n        log.Fatal(\"Lookup failed:\", err)\n    }\n}\nfmt.Println(\"Value:\", value)\n```\n\n### Update\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates an entry in the map. If the key already exists, its value is replaced. If the key doesn't exist, a new entry is created.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Thread-safe with write-locking\n- If caching is enabled:\n  - Adds/updates the cache entry\n  - Tracks the operation state (OK for success, Insert for error)\n  - Schedules an error resolver if the operation fails\n- Triggers event recording if events are enabled\n- Records metrics automatically\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 42}\nvalue := &MyValue{Count: 100}\nif err := m.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Update failed:\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Delete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes the entry with the given key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Returns an error if the key doesn't exist (use `SilentDelete()` to ignore missing keys)\n- Thread-safe with write-locking\n- If caching is enabled:\n  - Removes the entry from cache on success\n  - Updates the cache entry with error state on failure\n- Records metrics and events\n- Updates pressure metrics\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 42}\nif err := m.Delete(key); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Delete failed:\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### SilentDelete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n```\n\nDeletes the entry with the given key, but returns `(false, nil)` if the key doesn't exist instead of an error.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns `(true, nil)` if the key was successfully deleted\n- Returns `(false, nil)` if the key didn't exist\n- Returns `(false, err)` for actual errors\n\n**Use Case:**\n```go\n// Cleanup where keys might not exist\nif _, err := m.SilentDelete(key); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Delete error: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### DeleteLocked\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes an entry from within a DumpCallback. This method assumes the map lock is already held and must be called only from within callback functions passed to `DumpWithCallback()`, `DumpPerCPUWithCallback()`, or `DumpReliablyWithCallback()`.\n\n**Important:** Calling this from outside a callback will cause a deadlock.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Delete entries that match a condition\n    if shouldDelete(key, value) {\n        if err := m.DeleteLocked(key); err != nil {\n            log.Printf(\"Failed to delete %v: %v\", key, err)\n        }\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### DeleteAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nDeletes all entries from the map by iterating and deleting individual entries.\n\n**Behavioral Notes:**\n- Entries added concurrently while deletion is in progress may survive\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Thread-safe with write-locking\n- If caching is enabled:\n  - All cache entries are first marked for deletion\n  - Entries are updated as they are successfully deleted\n  - Error states are tracked in the cache\n- Records a `MapDeleteAll` event if events are enabled\n- Updates pressure metrics\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nif err := m.DeleteAll(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"DeleteAll failed:\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### ClearAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nSets all map entries to their zero values instead of deleting them. This is useful for maps where deletion is not applicable.\n\n**Constraints:**\n- Cannot be used with caching enabled\n- Cannot be used with events buffer enabled\n- Only works when both are disabled\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### Basic Iteration with DumpWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all entries in the map, calling the provided callback for each entry. This is the primary method for inspecting map contents.\n\n**Behavioral Details:**\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Creates fresh key and value objects for each iteration\n- Callback receives deep copies, safe to retain\n- Thread-safe with read-locking\n- Returns iteration errors from the underlying iterator\n\n**Constraints:**\n- Do not call Update/Delete directly in the callback (use `DeleteLocked()` for deletions)\n- Callback must not invoke map operations that require write lock\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nentries := make(map[string]string)\nerr := m.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    entries[key.String()] = value.String()\n})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Dump failed:\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Per-CPU Map Iteration\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over per-CPU maps, passing all CPU values for each key to the callback.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Map must be a per-CPU type (`ebpf.PerCPUHash`, `ebpf.PerCPUArray`, `ebpf.LRUCPUHash`, `ebpf.PerCPUCGroupStorage`)\n- Map value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue`\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := m.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    cpuValues := values.(*[]MyPerCPUValue)\n    for cpu, val := range *cpuValues {\n        fmt.Printf(\"CPU %d: %v\\n\", cpu, val)\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### Reliable Iteration with DumpReliablyWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nIterates over map entries with robust handling of concurrent modifications. If entries are deleted during iteration, the dump can resume from a previously-seen key rather than restarting.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Tracks recently-seen keys to recover from deletions\n- Limits iteration to 4× the map size to prevent infinite loops on continuously-modified maps\n- Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if this limit is exceeded\n- Acquires write lock (needed for callbacks that delete entries)\n\n**Stats Parameter:**\nThe stats object tracks iteration progress and is populated during the call:\n\n```go\ntype DumpStats struct {\n    Started       time.Time  // When iteration started\n    Finished      time.Time  // When iteration completed\n    Lookup        uint32     // Number of key lookups performed\n    LookupFailed  uint32     // Number of failed lookups\n    KeyFallback   uint32     // Times we fell back to previous key\n    MaxEntries    uint32     // Maximum map capacity\n    Interrupted   uint32     // Times iteration restarted\n    Completed     bool       // True if fully completed\n}\n\nfunc NewDumpStats(m *Map) *DumpStats\nfunc (d *DumpStats) Duration() time.Duration\n```\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Process entry\n}, stats)\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ErrMaxLookup) {\n        fmt.Printf(\"Iteration hit lookup limit after %d lookups\\n\", stats.Lookup)\n    }\n}\nfmt.Printf(\"Completed: %v, Duration: %v\\n\", stats.Completed, stats.Duration())\n```\n\n### Conditional Iteration\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nSame as `DumpWithCallback()` but returns early if the map doesn't exist on the filesystem, without returning an error.\n\n### Simple Map Dump\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nDumps all map entries into a `map[string][]string` for introspection. Values are converted to strings.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ndata := make(map[string][]string)\nif err := m.Dump(data); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Dump failed:\", err)\n}\nfor key, values := range data {\n    for _, val := range values {\n        fmt.Printf(\"%s => %s\\n\", key, val)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Batch Iterator API\n\n```go\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n    // ...\n}\n\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[...]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[...]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n\nfunc (bi BatchIterator[...]) Err() error\n```\n\nProvides efficient batched iteration of hash and LRU maps using the kernel's batch lookup API.\n\n**Type Parameters:**\n- `KT`: The key type (not a pointer)\n- `VT`: The value type (not a pointer)\n- `KP`: A pointer type to `KT` that implements `MapKey`\n- `VP`: A pointer type to `VT` that implements `MapValue`\n\n**Features:**\n- Automatically handles batch sizing\n- Retries on `ENOSPC` errors by doubling buffer size (default 3 retries)\n- Resets internal state on each `IterateAll()` call\n- Returns errors via `Err()` after iteration\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"test_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &TestKey{},\n    &TestValue{},\n    1000,\n    0,\n)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\niter := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.Background()) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", k, v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Iteration error: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n#### Batch Iterator Options\n\n```go\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[...](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\nfunc WithMaxRetries[...](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[...](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\n```\n\nCustomize batch iteration behavior:\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx,\n    WithStartingChunkSize[TestKey, TestValue](128),\n    WithMaxRetries[TestKey, TestValue](5),\n) {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Batch Count\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nUses batch lookup to count entries in hash and LRU maps efficiently.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Path Operations\n\n```go\n// Return the BPF filesystem root path (typically /sys/fs/bpf)\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n\n// Return the Cilium-specific path in bpffs (typically /sys/fs/bpf/cilium)\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n\n// Return the full path for a map name\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n\n// Create a directory in bpffs with correct permissions\nfunc MkdirBPF(path string) error\n\n// Remove a path, ignoring ErrNotExist\nfunc Remove(path string) error\n\n// Return legacy TC globals path\nfunc TCGlobalsPath() string\n```\n\n### Map Paths\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\nReturns the filesystem path where this map is pinned. If the path hasn't been set, it's automatically determined based on the map name and current configuration.\n\n### Pinning Maps\n\nMaps are automatically pinned when created with `OpenOrCreate()` or explicitly through collection loading. Pinning causes the kernel to create a reference to the map in the BPF filesystem, allowing it to be accessed and reused by other processes.\n\n**Automatic Pinning Behavior:**\n- Maps created with `OpenOrCreate()` are pinned by default\n- Maps created with `CreateUnpinned()` are not pinned\n- Maps are pinned at their derived path based on name\n\n### Unpinning Maps\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\nRemoves the map's pin from the filesystem.\n\n**Differences:**\n- `Unpin()`: Returns an error if the pin doesn't exist\n- `UnpinIfExists()`: Returns nil if the pin doesn't exist, only errors on actual issues\n\n**Note:** Unpinning does not delete the map itself—it only removes the filesystem reference. The map persists in the kernel until explicitly deleted or all references are closed.\n\n### Opening Existing Pinned Maps\n\n```go\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)\n```\n\nOpens a map that has already been pinned at the given absolute path. The path must be a valid absolute path to an existing pinned map.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- `pinPath` must be an absolute path\n- The map must already exist and be pinned\n- The key and value types must match the actual map\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nlogger := logging.DefaultSlogLogger\npath := MapPath(logger, \"cilium_ct_global\")\nm, err := OpenMap(path, &ConnectionKey{}, &ConnectionValue{})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Failed to open map:\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\n### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New returns a pointer to a new, zero-valued MapKey of the same type\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\nAll map keys must implement `MapKey`. Keys are used for:\n- Lookup, update, and delete operations\n- Iteration in callbacks\n- Comparison and hashing\n\n**Implementation Example:**\n\n```go\ntype MyKey struct {\n    ID        uint32\n    Namespace uint32\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"ID=%d NS=%d\", k.ID, k.Namespace)\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &MyKey{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New returns a pointer to a new, zero-valued MapValue of the same type\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\nAll map values must implement `MapValue`. Values are used for:\n- Lookup results\n- Update operations\n- Iteration callbacks\n\n**Implementation Example:**\n\n```go\ntype MyValue struct {\n    Packets uint64\n    Bytes   uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"Packets=%d Bytes=%d\", v.Packets, v.Bytes)\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyValue{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n\n    // NewSlice returns a pointer to a slice of the value type\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\nImplement `MapPerCPUValue` for values in per-CPU maps. The `NewSlice()` method must return a pointer to a slice of the value struct.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntype PerCPUStats struct {\n    Count uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"Count=%d\", v.Count)\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) New() MapValue {\n    return &PerCPUStats{}\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) NewSlice() any {\n    return &[]PerCPUStats{}\n}\n```\n\n### Concrete Example: EndpointKey\n\n```go\n// Represents an endpoint identified by its IP address\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6 // Stores IPv4 in lowest 4 bytes\n    Family    uint8      // EndpointKeyIPv4 or EndpointKeyIPv6\n    Key       uint8      // Typically 0\n    ClusterID uint16     // Cluster identifier\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    if addr := k.ToAddr(); addr.IsValid() {\n        return fmt.Sprintf(\"%s:%d\", addr, k.Key)\n    }\n    return \"nil\"\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n\nfunc NewEndpointKey(addr netip.Addr, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey {\n    result := EndpointKey{}\n    if addr.Is4() {\n        result.Family = EndpointKeyIPv4\n    } else if addr.Is6() {\n        result.Family = EndpointKeyIPv6\n    }\n    copy(result.IP[:], addr.AsSlice())\n    result.ClusterID = clusterID\n    return result\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\neBPF maps can record all operations (updates, deletes) to an event buffer for auditing and debugging. Events are recorded in a bounded ring buffer and can be dumped and/or subscribed to in real-time.\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables event recording for the map. The configuration specifies:\n- `Enabled`: Whether events are enabled\n- `MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to buffer\n- `TTL`: Time-to-live for events (0 = no expiration)\n\n**Memory Usage:**\nApproximately 100MB per million capacity.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_ct\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 100000, 0).\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 10000,\n        TTL:     time.Hour,\n    })\n```\n\n### Event Types\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate   Action = iota  // Entry was updated\n    MapDelete                  // Entry was deleted\n    MapDeleteAll               // All entries were deleted (aggregated event)\n)\n\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp      time.Time\n    Key            MapKey     // nil for MapDeleteAll\n    Value          MapValue   // nil for MapDelete and MapDeleteAll\n    DesiredAction  DesiredAction\n    LastError      error\n}\n\nfunc (e *Event) GetAction() string\nfunc (e Event) GetKey() string\nfunc (e Event) GetValue() string\nfunc (e Event) GetLastError() error\nfunc (e Event) GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction\n```\n\n### Querying Event Status\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nChecks if the event buffer is enabled for this map.\n\n### Dumping and Subscribing to Events\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool)\n```\n\nDumps existing events from the buffer and optionally subscribes to new events.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for managing the subscription lifetime\n- `callback`: Function called for each event\n- `follow`: If true, subscribe to future events; if false, only dump existing\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Dump and subscribe occur atomically to prevent race conditions\n- Callback is invoked sequentially for each event\n- When `follow` is true, the subscription continues until context is cancelled\n- Subscription automatically cleans up when context is cancelled\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    switch e.GetAction() {\n    case \"update\":\n        fmt.Printf(\"Updated: %s = %s\\n\", e.GetKey(), e.GetValue())\n    case \"delete\":\n        fmt.Printf(\"Deleted: %s\\n\", e.GetKey())\n    case \"delete-all\":\n        fmt.Printf(\"All entries deleted\\n\")\n    }\n\n    if e.LastError != nil {\n        fmt.Printf(\"Error: %v\\n\", e.LastError)\n    }\n}, true) // true = subscribe to future events\n```\n\n### Event Lifecycle\n\nEvents are automatically added to the buffer when:\n1. `Update()` is called (creates `MapUpdate` events)\n2. `Delete()` or `DeleteLocked()` is called (creates `MapDelete` events)\n3. `DeleteAll()` is called (creates `MapDeleteAll` events)\n\nEvents include the state of the operation (desired action: `Insert`, `Delete`, or `OK`) and any error that occurred.\n\n**Event Expiration:**\nIf a TTL is configured, events older than the TTL are automatically removed by a background controller.\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nThe collection loading API allows loading entire eBPF programs and maps from compiled objects (ELF files) into the kernel.\n\n### LoadAndAssign\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads an eBPF collection and assigns loaded programs and maps to struct fields in the provided object.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Analyzes the target struct to determine which objects to keep\n- Loads the collection into the kernel\n- Assigns loaded programs/maps to matching struct fields\n- Returns a commit function that must be called after programs are attached\n- Writes verifier errors to stderr if verification fails\n\n**Returns:**\n- Commit function: Must be called after all programs are attached\n- Error: If loading or assignment fails\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntype Objects struct {\n    ToNetdev *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_to_netdev\"`\n    FromNetdev *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_from_netdev\"`\n    ConntrackMap *Map `ebpf:\"cilium_ct4_global\"`\n}\n\nvar objs Objects\nspec, err := ebpf.LoadCollectionSpec(\"bpf_prog.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\ncommit, err := LoadAndAssign(logger, &objs, spec, nil)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// Attach programs to hooks\nif err := attachPrograms(&objs); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// Commit map pins\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### LoadCollection\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLower-level function that loads a collection without assignment. Returns the raw `ebpf.Collection` and a commit function.\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants for DECLARE_CONFIG runtime substitutions\n    Constants any\n\n    // Maps to rename during loading: key is spec key, value is new name\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // Maps to use as replacements for existing maps\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Objects to keep during reachability pruning\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // Path to write config dump for sysdumps\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Caching and Synchronization\n\nThe cache system allows Cilium to track the desired and actual state of map entries, useful for detecting and recovering from synchronization failures.\n\n### Enabling Cache\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map\n```\n\nEnables value caching for the map. Each entry is tracked with its desired state (Insert, Delete, or OK) and any errors that occurred.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Stores all inserted entries in a local cache\n- Tracks the operation status for each entry\n- Enables error resolution: failed operations are periodically retried\n- Integrates with pressure metrics\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_ct\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 10000, 0).\n    WithCache()\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### Cache Entry States\n\n```go\ntype DesiredAction uint8\n\nconst (\n    OK     DesiredAction = iota  // Entry is in sync\n    Insert                       // Entry needs to be inserted/updated\n    Delete                       // Entry needs to be deleted\n)\n```\n\nEach cached entry tracks:\n- **Key/Value**: The entry content\n- **DesiredAction**: The desired state (OK, Insert, or Delete)\n- **LastError**: Any error from the last operation\n\n### Error Resolution\n\nWhen an operation fails while caching is enabled:\n1. The entry is marked with the appropriate desired action\n2. An error resolver is scheduled\n3. The resolver periodically scans the cache and retries operations\n4. Successful operations update the entry to `OK` state\n\nThe resolver:\n- Runs periodically with configurable intervals\n- Limits scans to avoid excessive lock contention\n- Stops when all entries are synced\n\n### Map Model Export\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) GetModel() *models.BPFMap\n```\n\nReturns a representation of the map and its cache suitable for API export. If caching is enabled, includes cache entries with their states; otherwise, dumps map contents.\n\n---\n\n## Per-CPU Maps\n\nPer-CPU maps store different values on each CPU, useful for lock-free statistics and state.\n\n### Per-CPU Map Types\n\nSupported per-CPU map types:\n- `ebpf.PerCPUHash`\n- `ebpf.PerCPUArray`\n- `ebpf.LRUCPUHash`\n- `ebpf.PerCPUCGroupStorage`\n\n### Creating Per-CPU Maps\n\n```go\ntype CPUValue struct {\n    Packets uint64\n    Bytes   uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *CPUValue) String() string { ... }\nfunc (v *CPUValue) New() MapValue { return &CPUValue{} }\nfunc (v *CPUValue) NewSlice() any { return &[]CPUValue{} }\n\nm := NewMap(\"cpu_stats\",\n    ebpf.PerCPUHash,\n    &ConnKey{},\n    &CPUValue{},\n    10000,\n    0,\n)\n```\n\n### Iterating Per-CPU Maps\n\nPer-CPU maps require special iteration that retrieves all CPU values:\n\n```go\nm.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    cpuValues := values.(*[]CPUValue)\n    total := CPUValue{}\n    for _, v := range *cpuValues {\n        total.Packets += v.Packets\n        total.Bytes += v.Bytes\n    }\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key %s: total packets=%d, bytes=%d\\n\",\n        key, total.Packets, total.Bytes)\n})\n```\n\n---\n\n## Advanced Features\n\n### Metrics and Pressure Tracking\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map\nfunc (m *Map) UpdatePressureMetricWithSize(size int32)\n```\n\nTrack map pressure (ratio of used entries to capacity):\n- Automatically reported when pressure exceeds threshold\n- Useful for detecting maps approaching capacity\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"connections\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 100000, 0).\n    WithPressureMetric(metricsRegistry)\n```\n\n### Group Naming\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map\n```\n\nAssign a logical group name for metrics categorization.\n\n### NextKey Operations\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error\n```\n\nGets the next key after the given key in iteration order. Used internally by dump functions but available for advanced use cases.\n\n### Logging\n\nMaps include a structured logger accessible for custom logging:\n\n```go\nm.Logger.Info(\"Important event\", slog.String(\"detail\", \"value\"))\n```\n\n### Map Registration\n\nMaps are automatically registered internally for introspection:\n\n```go\nfunc registerMap(logger *slog.Logger, path string, m *Map)\nfunc unregisterMap(logger *slog.Logger, path string, m *Map)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Errors\n\n**`ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist`**\n- Returned by Lookup when key is not found\n- Expected error—check with `errors.Is()`\n\n**`ErrMaxLookup`**\n- Returned by `DumpReliablyWithCallback()` when iteration exceeds 4× max entries\n- Indicates map is being heavily modified during iteration\n\n**`ErrMapNotOpened`**\n- Returned by statedb reconciler operations if map isn't open\n\n**`unix.ENOSPC`**\n- Returned by batch operations when buffer is too small\n- Batch iterator automatically retries with larger buffer\n\n### Error Resolution Strategy\n\nFor operations with caching enabled:\n1. Operation failure triggers cache entry update\n2. Error resolver is scheduled for retry\n3. Resolver runs periodically until all entries sync\n4. Applications can check cache state via `GetModel()`\n\n---\n\n## Usage Patterns\n\n### Simple Map with CRUD\n\n```go\n// Create and open\nm := NewMap(\"test\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 1000, 0)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n\n// Operations\nkey := &Key{ID: 42}\nvalue := &Value{Count: 100}\n\nif err := m.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\nretrieved, _ := m.Lookup(key)\nfmt.Println(retrieved)\n\nm.Delete(key)\n```\n\n### Iteration with Processing\n\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Process each entry\n    fmt.Printf(\"%v: %v\\n\", key, value)\n}, stats)\n\nfmt.Printf(\"Completed=%v Lookups=%d Duration=%v\\n\",\n    stats.Completed, stats.Lookup, stats.Duration())\n```\n\n### Event Monitoring\n\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 60*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\n\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    log.Printf(\"Event: %s %s = %s (%v)\",\n        e.GetAction(), e.GetKey(), e.GetValue(), e.GetLastError())\n}, true)\n```\n\n### Batch Iteration\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[Key, Value](m)\ncount := 0\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.Background()) {\n    count++\n    // Process k and v\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Iteration failed after %d entries: %v\", count, err)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Thread Safety\n\nThe Map API is thread-safe:\n- Read operations (Lookup, iteration) use read locks\n- Write operations (Update, Delete) use write locks\n- All locks are automatically managed\n- CallBacks in dump operations hold appropriate locks\n\nImportant: Do not invoke blocking operations within callbacks or hold external locks when calling map methods, as this can cause deadlocks.\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Cilium eBPF Map API provides a complete, thread-safe interface for managing kernel eBPF maps from Go. With support for caching, events, metrics, pinning, and robust iteration, it handles the complexity of eBPF map lifecycle management while providing both convenience functions and low-level control for advanced use cases.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1109,"cache_read_input_tokens":66933,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1109},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"4689974f-7f1f-41a5-9dcc-690afe27faa2","uuid":"ab512ebb-2f95-48d1-8711-f10a610207ee"}

The `Map` type is the primary interface for all map operations, wrapping the lower-level ebpf-go library with Cilium-specific functionality including caching, event streaming, pinning, and metrics.\n\nAll eBPF maps are stored in a BPF filesystem (bpffs) and can be persisted between program runs through pinning.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Core Map Type and Creation](#core-map-type-and-creation)\n2. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n3. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n4. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n5. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n6. [Event System](#event-system)\n7. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n8. [Caching and Synchronization](#caching-and-synchronization)\n9. [Per-CPU Maps](#per-cpu-maps)\n10. [Advanced Features](#advanced-features)\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Type and Creation\n\n### Map Structure\n\nThe `Map` type is the main interface for working with eBPF maps:\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    Logger *slog.Logger\n    // ... internal fields\n}\n```\n\n#### Map Type Queries\n\n```go\n// Type returns the eBPF map type (Hash, LRUHash, Array, etc.)\nfunc (m *Map) Type() ebpf.MapType\n\n// KeySize returns the size of map keys in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) KeySize() uint32\n\n// ValueSize returns the size of map values in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) ValueSize() uint32\n\n// MaxEntries returns the maximum capacity of the map\nfunc (m *Map) MaxEntries() uint32\n\n// Flags returns the map creation flags\nfunc (m *Map) Flags() uint32\n\n// Name returns the basename of this map\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string\n\n// FD returns the file descriptor of the opened map\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int\n\n// IsOpen returns whether the map has been opened\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\n### Creating Maps\n\n#### NewMap\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new Map instance with the given parameters. The map is not yet created in the kernel; it remains in an uninitialized state until `Open()`, `OpenOrCreate()`, or `Create()` is called.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: The map name used for pinning and identification\n- `mapType`: The eBPF map type (e.g., `ebpf.Hash`, `ebpf.LRUHash`, `ebpf.Array`)\n- `mapKey`: A pointer to a sample map key (implements `MapKey`)\n- `mapValue`: A pointer to a sample map value (implements `MapValue`)\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum capacity of the map\n- `flags`: Creation flags (e.g., `unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_connections\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &ConnectionKey{},\n    &ConnectionValue{},\n    10000,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n)\n```\n\n#### NewMapWithInnerSpec\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a map with an inner map specification, used for maps of maps (e.g., for tail calls).\n\n### Opening and Creating Maps\n\n#### Open\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens an existing pinned map from the filesystem. If the map doesn't exist or cannot be opened, an error is returned. This call is idempotent—calling it multiple times on an already-open map succeeds without error.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires exclusive write lock for serialization\n- Loads the map from its pinned path\n- Automatically sets up metrics collection\n- Registers the map internally\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Failed to open map:\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n#### OpenOrCreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nAttempts to open an existing pinned map. If the map doesn't exist, creates and pins it. If an existing map is found but its attributes (type, key size, value size, capacity, flags) are incompatible, the old map is deleted and recreated.\n\n**Behavioral Details:**\n- Returns nil if the map was already open\n- Maps marked as non-persistent are always recreated\n- Automatically adds memory allocation flags based on map type\n- Sets `ebpf.PinByName` pinning flag during creation\n- Consumes the MapSpec after successful creation (cannot be reused)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\n// Create or reuse existing map\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Failed to open or create map:\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n#### Create\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nSimilar to `OpenOrCreate()` but closes the map after creation. Use this when you only need to create the map for initialization but don't intend to use it immediately.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `OpenOrCreate()` internally\n- Closes the map after successful creation\n- Useful for map initialization in startup hooks\n\n#### CreateUnpinned\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates the map without pinning it to the filesystem. The map exists only for the lifetime of the process.\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Temporary maps used only within a single process\n- Maps created for testing\n- Maps that are not meant to persist across restarts\n\n#### Recreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves any pinned map at the map's path, then creates and re-pins a new map. This is useful for forcing a fresh start of a map, clearing all previous entries.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Fails if the map is already open\n- Removes the old pin if it exists\n- Creates a new map and pins it\n\n**Example:**\n```go\n// Start fresh, discarding any previous entries\nif err := m.Recreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Failed to recreate map:\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n#### Close\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the map, releasing the file descriptor and unregistering it internally. After calling Close(), the map can be reopened by calling Open() or OpenOrCreate() again.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Idempotent—closing an already-closed map succeeds\n- Stops any active error resolution controller if caching is enabled\n- Unregisters the map from internal tracking\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nRetrieves the value associated with the given key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if the key is not found\n- Thread-safe with read-locking\n- Metrics collection is automatic if enabled\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 42}\nvalue, err := m.Lookup(key)\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n        fmt.Println(\"Key not found\")\n    } else {\n        log.Fatal(\"Lookup failed:\", err)\n    }\n}\nfmt.Println(\"Value:\", value)\n```\n\n### Update\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates an entry in the map. If the key already exists, its value is replaced. If the key doesn't exist, a new entry is created.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Thread-safe with write-locking\n- If caching is enabled:\n  - Adds/updates the cache entry\n  - Tracks the operation state (OK for success, Insert for error)\n  - Schedules an error resolver if the operation fails\n- Triggers event recording if events are enabled\n- Records metrics automatically\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 42}\nvalue := &MyValue{Count: 100}\nif err := m.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Update failed:\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Delete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes the entry with the given key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Returns an error if the key doesn't exist (use `SilentDelete()` to ignore missing keys)\n- Thread-safe with write-locking\n- If caching is enabled:\n  - Removes the entry from cache on success\n  - Updates the cache entry with error state on failure\n- Records metrics and events\n- Updates pressure metrics\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 42}\nif err := m.Delete(key); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Delete failed:\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### SilentDelete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n```\n\nDeletes the entry with the given key, but returns `(false, nil)` if the key doesn't exist instead of an error.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns `(true, nil)` if the key was successfully deleted\n- Returns `(false, nil)` if the key didn't exist\n- Returns `(false, err)` for actual errors\n\n**Use Case:**\n```go\n// Cleanup where keys might not exist\nif _, err := m.SilentDelete(key); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Delete error: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### DeleteLocked\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes an entry from within a DumpCallback. This method assumes the map lock is already held and must be called only from within callback functions passed to `DumpWithCallback()`, `DumpPerCPUWithCallback()`, or `DumpReliablyWithCallback()`.\n\n**Important:** Calling this from outside a callback will cause a deadlock.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Delete entries that match a condition\n    if shouldDelete(key, value) {\n        if err := m.DeleteLocked(key); err != nil {\n            log.Printf(\"Failed to delete %v: %v\", key, err)\n        }\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### DeleteAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nDeletes all entries from the map by iterating and deleting individual entries.\n\n**Behavioral Notes:**\n- Entries added concurrently while deletion is in progress may survive\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Thread-safe with write-locking\n- If caching is enabled:\n  - All cache entries are first marked for deletion\n  - Entries are updated as they are successfully deleted\n  - Error states are tracked in the cache\n- Records a `MapDeleteAll` event if events are enabled\n- Updates pressure metrics\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nif err := m.DeleteAll(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"DeleteAll failed:\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### ClearAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nSets all map entries to their zero values instead of deleting them. This is useful for maps where deletion is not applicable.\n\n**Constraints:**\n- Cannot be used with caching enabled\n- Cannot be used with events buffer enabled\n- Only works when both are disabled\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### Basic Iteration with DumpWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all entries in the map, calling the provided callback for each entry. This is the primary method for inspecting map contents.\n\n**Behavioral Details:**\n- Automatically opens the map if not already open\n- Creates fresh key and value objects for each iteration\n- Callback receives deep copies, safe to retain\n- Thread-safe with read-locking\n- Returns iteration errors from the underlying iterator\n\n**Constraints:**\n- Do not call Update/Delete directly in the callback (use `DeleteLocked()` for deletions)\n- Callback must not invoke map operations that require write lock\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nentries := make(map[string]string)\nerr := m.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    entries[key.String()] = value.String()\n})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Dump failed:\", err)\n}\n```\n\n### Per-CPU Map Iteration\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over per-CPU maps, passing all CPU values for each key to the callback.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Map must be a per-CPU type (`ebpf.PerCPUHash`, `ebpf.PerCPUArray`, `ebpf.LRUCPUHash`, `ebpf.PerCPUCGroupStorage`)\n- Map value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue`\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := m.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    cpuValues := values.(*[]MyPerCPUValue)\n    for cpu, val := range *cpuValues {\n        fmt.Printf(\"CPU %d: %v\\n\", cpu, val)\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### Reliable Iteration with DumpReliablyWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nIterates over map entries with robust handling of concurrent modifications. If entries are deleted during iteration, the dump can resume from a previously-seen key rather than restarting.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Tracks recently-seen keys to recover from deletions\n- Limits iteration to 4× the map size to prevent infinite loops on continuously-modified maps\n- Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if this limit is exceeded\n- Acquires write lock (needed for callbacks that delete entries)\n\n**Stats Parameter:**\nThe stats object tracks iteration progress and is populated during the call:\n\n```go\ntype DumpStats struct {\n    Started       time.Time  // When iteration started\n    Finished      time.Time  // When iteration completed\n    Lookup        uint32     // Number of key lookups performed\n    LookupFailed  uint32     // Number of failed lookups\n    KeyFallback   uint32     // Times we fell back to previous key\n    MaxEntries    uint32     // Maximum map capacity\n    Interrupted   uint32     // Times iteration restarted\n    Completed     bool       // True if fully completed\n}\n\nfunc NewDumpStats(m *Map) *DumpStats\nfunc (d *DumpStats) Duration() time.Duration\n```\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Process entry\n}, stats)\nif err != nil {\n    if errors.Is(err, ErrMaxLookup) {\n        fmt.Printf(\"Iteration hit lookup limit after %d lookups\\n\", stats.Lookup)\n    }\n}\nfmt.Printf(\"Completed: %v, Duration: %v\\n\", stats.Completed, stats.Duration())\n```\n\n### Conditional Iteration\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nSame as `DumpWithCallback()` but returns early if the map doesn't exist on the filesystem, without returning an error.\n\n### Simple Map Dump\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nDumps all map entries into a `map[string][]string` for introspection. Values are converted to strings.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ndata := make(map[string][]string)\nif err := m.Dump(data); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Dump failed:\", err)\n}\nfor key, values := range data {\n    for _, val := range values {\n        fmt.Printf(\"%s => %s\\n\", key, val)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Batch Iterator API\n\n```go\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n    // ...\n}\n\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[...]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[...]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n\nfunc (bi BatchIterator[...]) Err() error\n```\n\nProvides efficient batched iteration of hash and LRU maps using the kernel's batch lookup API.\n\n**Type Parameters:**\n- `KT`: The key type (not a pointer)\n- `VT`: The value type (not a pointer)\n- `KP`: A pointer type to `KT` that implements `MapKey`\n- `VP`: A pointer type to `VT` that implements `MapValue`\n\n**Features:**\n- Automatically handles batch sizing\n- Retries on `ENOSPC` errors by doubling buffer size (default 3 retries)\n- Resets internal state on each `IterateAll()` call\n- Returns errors via `Err()` after iteration\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"test_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &TestKey{},\n    &TestValue{},\n    1000,\n    0,\n)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\niter := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.Background()) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", k, v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Iteration error: %v\", err)\n}\n```\n\n#### Batch Iterator Options\n\n```go\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[...](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\nfunc WithMaxRetries[...](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[...](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\n```\n\nCustomize batch iteration behavior:\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx,\n    WithStartingChunkSize[TestKey, TestValue](128),\n    WithMaxRetries[TestKey, TestValue](5),\n) {\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Batch Count\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nUses batch lookup to count entries in hash and LRU maps efficiently.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Path Operations\n\n```go\n// Return the BPF filesystem root path (typically /sys/fs/bpf)\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n\n// Return the Cilium-specific path in bpffs (typically /sys/fs/bpf/cilium)\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n\n// Return the full path for a map name\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n\n// Create a directory in bpffs with correct permissions\nfunc MkdirBPF(path string) error\n\n// Remove a path, ignoring ErrNotExist\nfunc Remove(path string) error\n\n// Return legacy TC globals path\nfunc TCGlobalsPath() string\n```\n\n### Map Paths\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\nReturns the filesystem path where this map is pinned. If the path hasn't been set, it's automatically determined based on the map name and current configuration.\n\n### Pinning Maps\n\nMaps are automatically pinned when created with `OpenOrCreate()` or explicitly through collection loading. Pinning causes the kernel to create a reference to the map in the BPF filesystem, allowing it to be accessed and reused by other processes.\n\n**Automatic Pinning Behavior:**\n- Maps created with `OpenOrCreate()` are pinned by default\n- Maps created with `CreateUnpinned()` are not pinned\n- Maps are pinned at their derived path based on name\n\n### Unpinning Maps\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\nRemoves the map's pin from the filesystem.\n\n**Differences:**\n- `Unpin()`: Returns an error if the pin doesn't exist\n- `UnpinIfExists()`: Returns nil if the pin doesn't exist, only errors on actual issues\n\n**Note:** Unpinning does not delete the map itself—it only removes the filesystem reference. The map persists in the kernel until explicitly deleted or all references are closed.\n\n### Opening Existing Pinned Maps\n\n```go\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)\n```\n\nOpens a map that has already been pinned at the given absolute path. The path must be a valid absolute path to an existing pinned map.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- `pinPath` must be an absolute path\n- The map must already exist and be pinned\n- The key and value types must match the actual map\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nlogger := logging.DefaultSlogLogger\npath := MapPath(logger, \"cilium_ct_global\")\nm, err := OpenMap(path, &ConnectionKey{}, &ConnectionValue{})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(\"Failed to open map:\", err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\n### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New returns a pointer to a new, zero-valued MapKey of the same type\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\nAll map keys must implement `MapKey`. Keys are used for:\n- Lookup, update, and delete operations\n- Iteration in callbacks\n- Comparison and hashing\n\n**Implementation Example:**\n\n```go\ntype MyKey struct {\n    ID        uint32\n    Namespace uint32\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"ID=%d NS=%d\", k.ID, k.Namespace)\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &MyKey{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New returns a pointer to a new, zero-valued MapValue of the same type\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\nAll map values must implement `MapValue`. Values are used for:\n- Lookup results\n- Update operations\n- Iteration callbacks\n\n**Implementation Example:**\n\n```go\ntype MyValue struct {\n    Packets uint64\n    Bytes   uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"Packets=%d Bytes=%d\", v.Packets, v.Bytes)\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyValue{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n\n    // NewSlice returns a pointer to a slice of the value type\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\nImplement `MapPerCPUValue` for values in per-CPU maps. The `NewSlice()` method must return a pointer to a slice of the value struct.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntype PerCPUStats struct {\n    Count uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"Count=%d\", v.Count)\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) New() MapValue {\n    return &PerCPUStats{}\n}\n\nfunc (v *PerCPUStats) NewSlice() any {\n    return &[]PerCPUStats{}\n}\n```\n\n### Concrete Example: EndpointKey\n\n```go\n// Represents an endpoint identified by its IP address\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6 // Stores IPv4 in lowest 4 bytes\n    Family    uint8      // EndpointKeyIPv4 or EndpointKeyIPv6\n    Key       uint8      // Typically 0\n    ClusterID uint16     // Cluster identifier\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    if addr := k.ToAddr(); addr.IsValid() {\n        return fmt.Sprintf(\"%s:%d\", addr, k.Key)\n    }\n    return \"nil\"\n}\n\nfunc (k *EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n\nfunc NewEndpointKey(addr netip.Addr, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey {\n    result := EndpointKey{}\n    if addr.Is4() {\n        result.Family = EndpointKeyIPv4\n    } else if addr.Is6() {\n        result.Family = EndpointKeyIPv6\n    }\n    copy(result.IP[:], addr.AsSlice())\n    result.ClusterID = clusterID\n    return result\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\neBPF maps can record all operations (updates, deletes) to an event buffer for auditing and debugging. Events are recorded in a bounded ring buffer and can be dumped and/or subscribed to in real-time.\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables event recording for the map. The configuration specifies:\n- `Enabled`: Whether events are enabled\n- `MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to buffer\n- `TTL`: Time-to-live for events (0 = no expiration)\n\n**Memory Usage:**\nApproximately 100MB per million capacity.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_ct\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 100000, 0).\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n        Enabled: true,\n        MaxSize: 10000,\n        TTL:     time.Hour,\n    })\n```\n\n### Event Types\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate   Action = iota  // Entry was updated\n    MapDelete                  // Entry was deleted\n    MapDeleteAll               // All entries were deleted (aggregated event)\n)\n\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp      time.Time\n    Key            MapKey     // nil for MapDeleteAll\n    Value          MapValue   // nil for MapDelete and MapDeleteAll\n    DesiredAction  DesiredAction\n    LastError      error\n}\n\nfunc (e *Event) GetAction() string\nfunc (e Event) GetKey() string\nfunc (e Event) GetValue() string\nfunc (e Event) GetLastError() error\nfunc (e Event) GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction\n```\n\n### Querying Event Status\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nChecks if the event buffer is enabled for this map.\n\n### Dumping and Subscribing to Events\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool)\n```\n\nDumps existing events from the buffer and optionally subscribes to new events.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for managing the subscription lifetime\n- `callback`: Function called for each event\n- `follow`: If true, subscribe to future events; if false, only dump existing\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Dump and subscribe occur atomically to prevent race conditions\n- Callback is invoked sequentially for each event\n- When `follow` is true, the subscription continues until context is cancelled\n- Subscription automatically cleans up when context is cancelled\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    switch e.GetAction() {\n    case \"update\":\n        fmt.Printf(\"Updated: %s = %s\\n\", e.GetKey(), e.GetValue())\n    case \"delete\":\n        fmt.Printf(\"Deleted: %s\\n\", e.GetKey())\n    case \"delete-all\":\n        fmt.Printf(\"All entries deleted\\n\")\n    }\n\n    if e.LastError != nil {\n        fmt.Printf(\"Error: %v\\n\", e.LastError)\n    }\n}, true) // true = subscribe to future events\n```\n\n### Event Lifecycle\n\nEvents are automatically added to the buffer when:\n1. `Update()` is called (creates `MapUpdate` events)\n2. `Delete()` or `DeleteLocked()` is called (creates `MapDelete` events)\n3. `DeleteAll()` is called (creates `MapDeleteAll` events)\n\nEvents include the state of the operation (desired action: `Insert`, `Delete`, or `OK`) and any error that occurred.\n\n**Event Expiration:**\nIf a TTL is configured, events older than the TTL are automatically removed by a background controller.\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nThe collection loading API allows loading entire eBPF programs and maps from compiled objects (ELF files) into the kernel.\n\n### LoadAndAssign\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads an eBPF collection and assigns loaded programs and maps to struct fields in the provided object.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Analyzes the target struct to determine which objects to keep\n- Loads the collection into the kernel\n- Assigns loaded programs/maps to matching struct fields\n- Returns a commit function that must be called after programs are attached\n- Writes verifier errors to stderr if verification fails\n\n**Returns:**\n- Commit function: Must be called after all programs are attached\n- Error: If loading or assignment fails\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\ntype Objects struct {\n    ToNetdev *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_to_netdev\"`\n    FromNetdev *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_from_netdev\"`\n    ConntrackMap *Map `ebpf:\"cilium_ct4_global\"`\n}\n\nvar objs Objects\nspec, err := ebpf.LoadCollectionSpec(\"bpf_prog.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\ncommit, err := LoadAndAssign(logger, &objs, spec, nil)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// Attach programs to hooks\nif err := attachPrograms(&objs); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// Commit map pins\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### LoadCollection\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLower-level function that loads a collection without assignment. Returns the raw `ebpf.Collection` and a commit function.\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants for DECLARE_CONFIG runtime substitutions\n    Constants any\n\n    // Maps to rename during loading: key is spec key, value is new name\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // Maps to use as replacements for existing maps\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Objects to keep during reachability pruning\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // Path to write config dump for sysdumps\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Caching and Synchronization\n\nThe cache system allows Cilium to track the desired and actual state of map entries, useful for detecting and recovering from synchronization failures.\n\n### Enabling Cache\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map\n```\n\nEnables value caching for the map. Each entry is tracked with its desired state (Insert, Delete, or OK) and any errors that occurred.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Stores all inserted entries in a local cache\n- Tracks the operation status for each entry\n- Enables error resolution: failed operations are periodically retried\n- Integrates with pressure metrics\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"cilium_ct\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 10000, 0).\n    WithCache()\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### Cache Entry States\n\n```go\ntype DesiredAction uint8\n\nconst (\n    OK     DesiredAction = iota  // Entry is in sync\n    Insert                       // Entry needs to be inserted/updated\n    Delete                       // Entry needs to be deleted\n)\n```\n\nEach cached entry tracks:\n- **Key/Value**: The entry content\n- **DesiredAction**: The desired state (OK, Insert, or Delete)\n- **LastError**: Any error from the last operation\n\n### Error Resolution\n\nWhen an operation fails while caching is enabled:\n1. The entry is marked with the appropriate desired action\n2. An error resolver is scheduled\n3. The resolver periodically scans the cache and retries operations\n4. Successful operations update the entry to `OK` state\n\nThe resolver:\n- Runs periodically with configurable intervals\n- Limits scans to avoid excessive lock contention\n- Stops when all entries are synced\n\n### Map Model Export\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) GetModel() *models.BPFMap\n```\n\nReturns a representation of the map and its cache suitable for API export. If caching is enabled, includes cache entries with their states; otherwise, dumps map contents.\n\n---\n\n## Per-CPU Maps\n\nPer-CPU maps store different values on each CPU, useful for lock-free statistics and state.\n\n### Per-CPU Map Types\n\nSupported per-CPU map types:\n- `ebpf.PerCPUHash`\n- `ebpf.PerCPUArray`\n- `ebpf.LRUCPUHash`\n- `ebpf.PerCPUCGroupStorage`\n\n### Creating Per-CPU Maps\n\n```go\ntype CPUValue struct {\n    Packets uint64\n    Bytes   uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *CPUValue) String() string { ... }\nfunc (v *CPUValue) New() MapValue { return &CPUValue{} }\nfunc (v *CPUValue) NewSlice() any { return &[]CPUValue{} }\n\nm := NewMap(\"cpu_stats\",\n    ebpf.PerCPUHash,\n    &ConnKey{},\n    &CPUValue{},\n    10000,\n    0,\n)\n```\n\n### Iterating Per-CPU Maps\n\nPer-CPU maps require special iteration that retrieves all CPU values:\n\n```go\nm.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    cpuValues := values.(*[]CPUValue)\n    total := CPUValue{}\n    for _, v := range *cpuValues {\n        total.Packets += v.Packets\n        total.Bytes += v.Bytes\n    }\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key %s: total packets=%d, bytes=%d\\n\",\n        key, total.Packets, total.Bytes)\n})\n```\n\n---\n\n## Advanced Features\n\n### Metrics and Pressure Tracking\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map\nfunc (m *Map) UpdatePressureMetricWithSize(size int32)\n```\n\nTrack map pressure (ratio of used entries to capacity):\n- Automatically reported when pressure exceeds threshold\n- Useful for detecting maps approaching capacity\n\n```go\nm := NewMap(\"connections\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 100000, 0).\n    WithPressureMetric(metricsRegistry)\n```\n\n### Group Naming\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map\n```\n\nAssign a logical group name for metrics categorization.\n\n### NextKey Operations\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error\n```\n\nGets the next key after the given key in iteration order. Used internally by dump functions but available for advanced use cases.\n\n### Logging\n\nMaps include a structured logger accessible for custom logging:\n\n```go\nm.Logger.Info(\"Important event\", slog.String(\"detail\", \"value\"))\n```\n\n### Map Registration\n\nMaps are automatically registered internally for introspection:\n\n```go\nfunc registerMap(logger *slog.Logger, path string, m *Map)\nfunc unregisterMap(logger *slog.Logger, path string, m *Map)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Errors\n\n**`ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist`**\n- Returned by Lookup when key is not found\n- Expected error—check with `errors.Is()`\n\n**`ErrMaxLookup`**\n- Returned by `DumpReliablyWithCallback()` when iteration exceeds 4× max entries\n- Indicates map is being heavily modified during iteration\n\n**`ErrMapNotOpened`**\n- Returned by statedb reconciler operations if map isn't open\n\n**`unix.ENOSPC`**\n- Returned by batch operations when buffer is too small\n- Batch iterator automatically retries with larger buffer\n\n### Error Resolution Strategy\n\nFor operations with caching enabled:\n1. Operation failure triggers cache entry update\n2. Error resolver is scheduled for retry\n3. Resolver runs periodically until all entries sync\n4. Applications can check cache state via `GetModel()`\n\n---\n\n## Usage Patterns\n\n### Simple Map with CRUD\n\n```go\n// Create and open\nm := NewMap(\"test\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 1000, 0)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer m.Close()\n\n// Operations\nkey := &Key{ID: 42}\nvalue := &Value{Count: 100}\n\nif err := m.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\nretrieved, _ := m.Lookup(key)\nfmt.Println(retrieved)\n\nm.Delete(key)\n```\n\n### Iteration with Processing\n\n```go\nstats := NewDumpStats(m)\nerr := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    // Process each entry\n    fmt.Printf(\"%v: %v\\n\", key, value)\n}, stats)\n\nfmt.Printf(\"Completed=%v Lookups=%d Duration=%v\\n\",\n    stats.Completed, stats.Lookup, stats.Duration())\n```\n\n### Event Monitoring\n\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 60*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\n\nm.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(e Event) {\n    log.Printf(\"Event: %s %s = %s (%v)\",\n        e.GetAction(), e.GetKey(), e.GetValue(), e.GetLastError())\n}, true)\n```\n\n### Batch Iteration\n\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[Key, Value](m)\ncount := 0\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.Background()) {\n    count++\n    // Process k and v\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Printf(\"Iteration failed after %d entries: %v\", count, err)\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Thread Safety\n\nThe Map API is thread-safe:\n- Read operations (Lookup, iteration) use read locks\n- Write operations (Update, Delete) use write locks\n- All locks are automatically managed\n- CallBacks in dump operations hold appropriate locks\n\nImportant: Do not invoke blocking operations within callbacks or hold external locks when calling map methods, as this can cause deadlocks.\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Cilium eBPF Map API provides a complete, thread-safe interface for managing kernel eBPF maps from Go. With support for caching, events, metrics, pinning, and robust iteration, it handles the complexity of eBPF map lifecycle management while providing both convenience functions and low-level control for advanced use cases.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
